{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2021-04-03 12:48:46","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:48:46","title":"Our Greatest Misunderstanding About Love: Philosopher-Psychiatrist Esther Perel on Modern Loneliness as Ambiguous Loss and the Essential Elements of Healthy Relationships","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=73044","description":"<h3>On the lifelong art of feeling worthy of wanting and worthy of receiving. </h3>\n<hr>\n<p>In his revelatory 1956 classic <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/10/29/the-art-of-loving-erich-fromm/\"><em>The Art of Loving</em></a>, the humanistic philosopher and psychologist <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/tag/erich-fromm/\">Erich Fromm</a> (March 23, 1900&#8211;March 18, 1980) dared defy millennia of cultural distortion, setting out to heal our most damaging inheritance from the Romantics and to correct Freud&#8217;s limited, limiting theories with a new lens on love, radical and realistic: For centuries, our culture conditioned us to <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/10/29/the-art-of-loving-erich-fromm/\">&#8220;see the problem of love primarily as that of being <em>loved</em>, rather than that of <em>loving</em>,&#8221;</a> which in turn conditioned us to believe that the hardest thing about love is finding the right person to love us, but once we do, love is easy. </p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/they-were-lonesome-from-trees-at-night-by-art-young_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/artyoung_treesatnight6.jpg?resize=680%2C1061&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1061\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-68435\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/artyoung_treesatnight6.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, The difficult work is the mastering, which then confers ease upon love between those who have done this work &#8212; the work which Rilke well knew <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/01/29/rilke-on-love/\">&#8220;is perhaps the most difficult of all our tasks… the work for which all other work is but preparation.&#8221;</a></p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_64208\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/how-calm-how-solemn-it-grows-to-ascend-the-atmosphere-of-lovers_print?sku=s6-8967910p4a1v45?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass10.jpg?resize=680%2C899&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"899\" class=\"size-full wp-image-64208\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass10.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass10.jpg?resize=240%2C317&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass10.jpg?resize=320%2C423&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass10.jpg?resize=768%2C1015&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass10.jpg?resize=600%2C793&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Margaret C. Cook from a <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/04/11/leaves-of-grass-margaret-cook/\">rare 1913 edition</a> of Walt Whitman&#8217;s <em>Leaves of Grass</em>. Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/how-calm-how-solemn-it-grows-to-ascend-the-atmosphere-of-lovers_print?sku=s6-8967910p4a1v45?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>An inheritor to Fromm&#8217;s work born a century after the publication his masterpiece, the Belgian-American philosopher-psychotherapist <strong>Esther Perel</strong> &#8212; author of the modern classic <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/10/13/mating-in-captivity-esther-perel/\"><em>Mating in Captivity</em></a>, creator of the insightful and pleasantly disquieting <a href=\"https://whereshouldwebegin.estherperel.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>Where Should We Begin?</em></a> &#8220;podcast for anyone who has ever loved&#8221; &#8212; picks up where Fromm left off in this lovely animated adaptation of her <a href=\"https://onbeing.org/programs/esther-perel-the-erotic-is-an-antidote-to-death/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>On Being</em> interview</a>, exploring the essential elements of love as a practice, the delicate relationship between play and risk, the cyclical nature of passion, the osmosis of desire and self-worth, and how the concept of ambiguous loss illuminates the modern experience of loneliness: </p>\n<p><iframe loading=\"lazy\" title=\"The Esther Perel Love Lexicon\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/fij1QGBIjg8?feature=oembed&#38;rel=0&#38;controls=0&#38;showinfo=0&#38;iv_load_policy=3\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>Complement with Fromm on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/04/27/erich-fromm-sane-society-self-love/\">what self-love really means</a>, his <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/04/05/erich-fromm-the-art-of-listening/\">six rules of intimate listening</a>, and Alain de Botton on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/12/09/alain-de-botton-school-of-life-love/\">remedying our central error of logic in love</a>, then broaden the lens with an ancient Eastern perspective in the great Zen Buddhism teacher Thich Nhat Hanh&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/03/31/how-to-love-thich-nhat-hanh/\">field guide to the skill of loving</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. The boundaries between our bodies begin to dissolve here&#8230; Immunity&#8230; is a common trust as much as it is a private account.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Immunity-Inoculation-Eula-Biss/dp/1555976891/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"480\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/eulabiss_onimmunity.jpg?fit=320%2C480&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover with-border alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Immunity, Interdependence, and the Shared Root of Our Safety and Our Sanity: Eula Biss on the Science and Social Dynamics of Health as Communal Trust\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/eulabiss_onimmunity.jpg?w=1400&#38;ssl=1 1400w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/eulabiss_onimmunity.jpg?resize=320%2C480&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/eulabiss_onimmunity.jpg?resize=600%2C900&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/eulabiss_onimmunity.jpg?resize=240%2C360&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/eulabiss_onimmunity.jpg?resize=768%2C1152&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/eulabiss_onimmunity.jpg?resize=1024%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1024w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/eulabiss_onimmunity.jpg?resize=1365%2C2048&#38;ssl=1 1365w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>Months after Rachel Carson&#8217;s <em>Silent Spring</em> <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/01/27/rachel-carson-silent-spring-dorothy-freeman/\">awakened humanity to the delicate interdependence of nature</a>, Dr. King awakened humanity to our delicate dependence on each other. <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/03/18/martin-luther-king-letter-from-birmingham-city-jail/\">&#8220;We are caught in an inescapable network of mutuality [and] whatever affects one directly, affects all indirectly,”</a> he wrote from his cell at the Birmingham City Jail.</p>\n<p>When Robert Hooke looked at a piece of cork through an early handcrafted leather-and-gold microscope in 1665, he named the strange irregular &#8220;pores&#8221; of its honeycomb-like tissue structure <em>cells</em>, after the small adjacent spaces in which monks spend their voluntary solitary confinement. It would take another two centuries for scientists to discover that cells are the basic biological units of life, that they are in constant osmotic communication with one another, and that they replicate themselves to become new cells, each a whispered word from the language in which life talks to the future.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73004\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/cork-structure-from-robert-hookes-micrographia-1665_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/RobertHooke_Micrographia_cork.jpg?resize=680%2C1007&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1007\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73004\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/RobertHooke_Micrographia_cork.jpg?w=1080&#38;ssl=1 1080w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/RobertHooke_Micrographia_cork.jpg?resize=320%2C474&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/RobertHooke_Micrographia_cork.jpg?resize=600%2C889&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/RobertHooke_Micrographia_cork.jpg?resize=240%2C356&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/RobertHooke_Micrographia_cork.jpg?resize=768%2C1138&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/RobertHooke_Micrographia_cork.jpg?resize=1037%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1037w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Cork structure from Robert Hooke&#8217;s <em>Micrographia</em>, 1665. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/cork-structure-from-robert-hookes-micrographia-1665_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Biological and social, our interdependence is a defining feature not only of our civilization, not only of our species and all living species, but of life itself &#8212; life the physiological process and life the psychosocial phenomenon. <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/10/19/lia-halloran-walt-whitman-universe-in-verse/\">&#8220;Every atom belonging to me as good belongs to you,&#8221;</a> Walt Whitman exulted in the golden age of chemistry &#8212; the new science he saw as &#8220;the elevating, beautiful, study&#8230; which involves the essences of creation.&#8221; Meanwhile, the development of cell theory was revolutionizing biology, making of this philosophical field as old as Aristotle an even newer science that illuminated the essence of life. Cells became to biology what atoms were to chemistry. Biology ushered in the revelation that every cell belonging to me as good &#8212; as healthy, as vital, as fit for replication &#8212; belongs to you.  </p>\n<p>That delicate interdependence of life and lives, with its tangled roots in biology and cultural history, is what <strong>Eula Biss</strong> explores in <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Immunity-Inoculation-Eula-Biss/dp/1555976891/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>On Immunity: An Inoculation</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/on-immunity-an-inoculation/oclc/1146587404&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; a book of penetrating and poetic insight, drawn with that rare scholarship capable of correcting the warped cultural hindsight we call history; a book of staggering foresight, conceived in the wake of the H1N1 flu pandemic, yet speaking with astonishing prescience to the complex epidemiological realities and social dynamics of the COVID-19 pandemic unfolding more than five years after its publication.   </p>\n<p>For Biss &#8212; the daughter of a medical scientist and a poet &#8212; even her own biological inheritance as a universal donor with type O negative blood becomes a potent metaphor for the mechanism of vaccination, a lens through which to view the permeable membrane between the biological and social realities of immunity. With an eye to the blood banks that collect her donations to save other lives, she writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>If we imagine the action of a vaccine not just in terms of how it affects a single body, but also in terms of how it affects the collective body of a community, it is fair to think of vaccination as a kind of banking of immunity. Contributions to this bank are donations to those who cannot or will not be protected by their own immunity. This is the principle of <em>herd immunity</em>, and it is through herd immunity that mass vaccination becomes far more effective than individual vaccination.</p></blockquote>\n<p>It is a rather unfortunate term for an unassailable scientific principle &#8212; we humans, especially in this culture of rugged individualism nursed on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/04/06/emerson-self-reliance/\">the Emersonian ideal of self-reliance</a>, bristle at thinking of ourselves as members of a herd. In our <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/04/16/thinking-with-animals-lorainne-daston-gregg-mitman/\">long history of thinking with animals</a>, herd animals have been the butt of our derogatory metaphors for mindless conformity. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_49569\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/10/14/louis-i-king-of-the-sheep-olivier-tallec/\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2015/10/louisi_tallec00.jpg?w=680&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Art by Olivier Tallec from Louis I, King of the Sheep\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Olivier Tallec from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/10/14/louis-i-king-of-the-sheep-olivier-tallec/\"><em>Louis I, King of the Sheep</em></a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>And yet inside the unfortunate linguistic container, an unfaltering biological reality resides: On large enough a scale, even a fairy ineffective vaccine that fails to produce immunity in some individuals will slow down the spread of infection in the community; as the virus fails to replicate itself in more and more new hosts, the vaccine will eventually halt it altogether. In consequence, even such a mediocre vaccine will protect all members of the community, even those for whom inoculation has not worked as intended on the individual level. This is why it is more dangerous to be the vaccinated animal amid a largely unvaccinated herd than the other way around. Biss writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The unvaccinated person is protected by the bodies around her, bodies through which disease is not circulating. But a vaccinated person surrounded by bodies that host disease is left vulnerable to vaccine failure or fading immunity. We are protected not so much by our own skin, but by what is beyond it. The boundaries between our bodies begin to dissolve here. Donations of blood and organs move between us, exiting one body and entering another, and so too with immunity, which is a common trust as much as it is a private account. Those of us who draw on collective immunity owe our health to our neighbors.</p></blockquote>\n<p>With an eye to the origin of herd immunity theory &#8212; a theory developed in the 1840s by a doctor treating smallpox, which has taken manyfold more human lives than any other infectious disease in the history of our species and which has since been eradicated &#8212; Biss proposes an alternative, both more poetic and more precise, to the imperfect term that so perfectly describes the biosocial reality:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Herd immunity, an observable phenomenon, now seems implausible only if we think of our bodies as inherently disconnected from other bodies. Which, of course, we do. </p>\n<p>The very expression <em>herd immunity</em> suggests that we are cattle, waiting, perhaps, to be sent to slaughter. And it invites an unfortunate association with the term <em>herd mentality</em>, a stampede toward stupidity. The herd, we assume, is foolish. Those of us who eschew the herd mentality tend to prefer a frontier mentality in which we imagine our bodies as isolated homesteads that we tend either well or badly. The health of the homestead next to ours does not affect us, this thinking suggests, so long as ours is well tended. </p>\n<p>If we were to exchange the metaphor of the herd for a hive, perhaps the concept of shared immunity might be more appealing. Honeybees are matriarchal, environmental do-gooders who also happen to be entirely interdependent. The health of any individual bee, as we know from the recent epidemic of colony collapse, depends on the health of the hive.</p></blockquote>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/paul-sougy-the-bee-1962-proceeds-benefit-the-nature-conservancy_print?sku=s6-11999106p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/sougy_bee.jpg?resize=680%2C879&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"879\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-69321\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/sougy_bee.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/sougy_bee.jpg?resize=240%2C310&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/sougy_bee.jpg?resize=320%2C414&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/sougy_bee.jpg?resize=768%2C993&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/sougy_bee.jpg?resize=600%2C776&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Diagram of bee anatomy by French artist Paul Sougy, 1962. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/paul-sougy-the-bee-1962-proceeds-benefit-the-nature-conservancy_print?sku=s6-11999106p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Biss quotes a succinct summation by her father, a doctor:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Vaccination works by enlisting a majority in the protection of a minority.</p></blockquote>\n<p>No one person has done more to undermine this vital mutuality of protection than Andrew Wakefield &#8212; the British gastroenterologist who, in the 1990s, infected the hive mind with his causal claims linking vaccines and autism. Preying on the understandable human impulse toward concretizing blame for amorphous and ambiguous problems, the theory went viral before multiple subsequent studies debunked his results, before it was exposed that Wakefield was paid for his research by a lawyer readying a lawsuit against a vaccine maker, before the General Medical Council of the United Kingdom concluded its investigation with the verdict that Wakefield had been “irresponsible and dishonest” in conducting and publishing his work.</p>\n<p>Despite the scientific and ethical denunciation of Wakefield&#8217;s study, its ideological meme had already spread beyond retrieval. (Richard Dawkins coined the word <em>meme</em> in 1976 by <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/10/02/richard-dawkins-meme-appetite-for-wonder/\">borrowing from biology</a> &#8212; a word that came alive anew a quarter century later in the context of &#8220;viral&#8221; content on the internet, which has its own roots in epidemiology.) A quarter century later, echoes of Wakefield&#8217;s disproven falsehoods bellow with formidable vocality. That group of voices is often referred to as the anti-vaccination movement, but I find the term <em>movement</em> extremely ill-suited &#8212; such groupthink is not in movement but static, frozen in time and frozen with fear, petrified in the cultural amber of a time before the Age of Reason and lashed about by the same errors of magical thinking, willful blindness, and confusion of causation and correlation that made our medieval ancestors take comets for indisputable omens of future events and left-handedness for indisputable evidence of possession by the Devil. </p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-the-comet-book-15872417711_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/01/comet9.jpg?resize=680%2C798&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"798\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-59410\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/01/comet9.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/01/comet9.jpg?resize=240%2C282&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/01/comet9.jpg?resize=320%2C375&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/01/comet9.jpg?resize=768%2C901&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/01/comet9.jpg?resize=600%2C704&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/01/11/kometenbuch-the-comet-book/\"><em>The Comet Book</em></a>, 1587. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-the-comet-book-15872417711_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>).</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Biss is more generous in her own assessment of anti-vaccination:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Those who went on to use Wakefield’s inconclusive work to support the notion that vaccines cause autism are not guilty of ignorance or science denial so much as they are guilty of using weak science as it has always been used &#8212; to lend false credibility to an idea that we want to believe for other reasons.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Writing shortly after the birth of the Occupy movement &#8212; the self-described &#8220;99%&#8221; launching &#8220;an ongoing global protest of capitalism&#8221; &#8212; she considers a friend&#8217;s half-joke, half-koan about vaccination as a matter of &#8220;occupy immune system,&#8221; and reflects on the basic moral syllogism of anti-vaccination as a political stance claiming to protest the capitalist forces behind modern medicine:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Immunity is a public space. And it can be occupied by those who choose not to carry immunity. For some&#8230; a refusal to vaccinate falls under a broader resistance to capitalism. But refusing immunity as a form of civil disobedience bears an unsettling resemblance to the very structure the Occupy movement seeks to disrupt &#8212; a privileged 1 percent are sheltered from risk while they draw resources from the other 99 percent.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>We are justified in feeling threatened by the unlimited expansion of industry, and we are justified in fearing that our interests are secondary to corporate interests. But refusal of vaccination undermines a system that is not actually typical of capitalism. It is a system in which both the burdens and the benefits are shared across the entire population. Vaccination allows us to use the products of capitalism for purposes that are counter to the pressures of capital.</p></blockquote>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/honeybee_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=680%2C680&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"680\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-73007\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/honeybee_MariaPopova.jpg?w=2362&#38;ssl=1 2362w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/honeybee_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=320%2C320&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/honeybee_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/honeybee_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=240%2C240&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/honeybee_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=768%2C768&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/honeybee_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=1536%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1536w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/honeybee_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=2048%2C2048&#38;ssl=1 2048w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/honeybee_MariaPopova.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Emissary</em> by Maria Popova</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In a lovely antidote to the tragic human tendency toward cynicism &#8212; that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/02/09/hope-cynicism/\"> touchingly misguided and ineffective effort at self-protection</a>, that particularly virulent <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/09/21/caitlin-moran-cynicism/\">strain of cowardice</a> to which our culture has grown increasingly hospitable as it has grown increasingly impatient with the slow and vulnerable work of nuance &#8212; Biss adds:</p>\n<blockquote><p>That so many of us find it entirely plausible that a vast network of researchers and health officials and doctors worldwide would willfully harm children for money is evidence of what capitalism is really taking from us. Capitalism has already impoverished the working people who generate wealth for others. And capitalism has already impoverished us culturally, robbing unmarketable art of its value. But when we begin to see the pressures of capitalism as innate laws of human motivation, when we begin to believe that everyone is owned, then we are truly impoverished.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Complement <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Immunity-Inoculation-Eula-Biss/dp/1555976891/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>On Immunity</em></strong></a> &#8212; a redemptive and salutary read in its entirety &#8212; with Virginia Woolf on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/05/06/virginia-woolf-on-being-ill/\">illness as a portal to self-understanding</a> and Bessel van der Kolk on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/06/20/the-body-keeps-the-score-van-der-kolk/\">the science of how our minds and our bodies converge in healing</a>, then revisit Adrienne Rich on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/05/19/adrienne-rich-arts-of-the-possible-capitalism/\">resisting capitalism through the arts of the possible</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your life more livable in any way, please consider aiding its sustenance with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/donate/\">donation</a>.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p>Brain Pickings has a free weekly newsletter. 12:48:46","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:48:46","title":"Seeking an Aurora: A Wondrous Illustrated Celebration of Earth’s Most Otherworldly Spectacle of Light and Color","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=73084","description":"<h3>Transcendence and tenderness in the lacuna of awe between the creaturely and the cosmic.</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Seeking-Aurora-Elizabeth-Pulford/dp/1733121277/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"373\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora-1.jpg?fit=320%2C373&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover-landscape alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Seeking an Aurora: A Wondrous Illustrated Celebration of Earth&#8217;s Most Otherworldly Spectacle of Light and Color\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora-1.jpg?w=1080&#38;ssl=1 1080w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora-1.jpg?resize=320%2C373&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora-1.jpg?resize=600%2C699&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora-1.jpg?resize=240%2C280&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora-1.jpg?resize=768%2C895&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>In 1621, already questioning his life in the priesthood &#8212; the era&#8217;s safest and most reputable career for the educated &#8212; the 29-year-old Pierre Gassendi, a mathematical prodigy since childhood, traveled to the Arctic circle as he began diverting his passionate erudition toward Aristotelian philosophy and astronomy. There, under the polar skies, he witnessed an otherworldly spectacle on Earth &#8212; our planet&#8217;s most intimate and dramatic contact with its home star, a chromatic swirl of the ephemeral and the eternal unloosed as solar winds blow millions of charged particles from the Sun across the orrery of the Solar System and into Earth&#8217;s atmosphere, where our magnetic fields carry them toward the poles. As they collide with the particles of different atmospheric gasses, they ionize and discharge energy as photons of different colors &#8212; red, blue, green, and violent &#8212; painting the nocturne with the waking dream of a pastel-technicolor dawn. </p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Seeking-Aurora-Elizabeth-Pulford/dp/1733121277/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora7.jpg?resize=680%2C468&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"468\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-73090\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora7.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora7.jpg?resize=320%2C220&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora7.jpg?resize=600%2C413&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora7.jpg?resize=240%2C165&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora7.jpg?resize=768%2C528&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p>Awestruck with the natural poetry and the mythic feeling-tone of the luminous spectacle, Gassendi named what he saw <em>Aurora borealis</em> &#8212; after Aurora, the Roman goddess of dawn, and <em>borealis</em>, the Latin word for &#8220;northern.&#8221; Eventually, as explorers braved the icy oceanic expanses to visit the polar regions of the Southern hemisphere over the following centuries, they adapted Gassendi&#8217;s etymology to name the Antarctic version of the luminous display <em>Aurora australis</em>, after the Latin word for &#8220;southern.&#8221;</p>\n<p>From the land of <em>Aurora australis</em> comes <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Seeking-Aurora-Elizabeth-Pulford/dp/1733121277/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Seeking an Aurora</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/seeking-an-aurora/oclc/1237827722&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; a work of transcendence and tenderness by New Zealand author-artist duo Elizabeth Pulford and Anne Bannock, whose spare poetic prose and soulful paintings interleave to enlush an inner landscape of wonder, suspended between the creaturely and the cosmic.</p>\n<p>Late one night, a father awakens his child &#8212; a child of ambiguous gender and ethnicity, a touching effort to approximate the universal in the human &#8212; to slip out of the house together, past the soundly sleeping mother and the baby in the crib, and out into the winter nocturne on a quest of wonder. </p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Seeking-Aurora-Elizabeth-Pulford/dp/1733121277/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora21.jpg?resize=680%2C449&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"449\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-73096\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora21.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora21.jpg?resize=320%2C211&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora21.jpg?resize=600%2C397&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora21.jpg?resize=240%2C159&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora21.jpg?resize=768%2C508&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Seeking-Aurora-Elizabeth-Pulford/dp/1733121277/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora1.jpg?resize=680%2C946&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"946\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-73091\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora1.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, /></a></p>\n<p>They walk with brisk excitation across the open field and through the skeletal trees as the warm humanity of their breath puffs into the cold night air, into the silence they share with the other breathing creatures that make this planet a world. </p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Seeking-Aurora-Elizabeth-Pulford/dp/1733121277/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora3.jpg?resize=680%2C486&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"486\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-73089\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora3.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, /></a></p>\n<blockquote><p>Outside everything was still.<br />\nEven the dogs were quiet, and the cows looked like prehistoric creatures, their noses streaming smoke.</p></blockquote>\n<p>The adventure unfolds from the narrative vantage point of the child, who turns around to look back at the house with its &#8220;warm, buttery light spilling from the kitchen window,&#8221; back at the two sets of &#8220;footprints in the silvery frost,&#8221; then up at the sky, &#8220;a ship of shivering stars.&#8221; </p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Seeking-Aurora-Elizabeth-Pulford/dp/1733121277/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora2.jpg?resize=680%2C491&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"491\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-73086\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora2.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora2.jpg?resize=768%2C555&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p>As the pair ascend the steep hill toward their lookout, the cows and the dogs recede into the distance, leaving only the stars, the Moon, and the swell of anticipation. </p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Seeking-Aurora-Elizabeth-Pulford/dp/1733121277/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora4.jpg?resize=680%2C474&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"474\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-73087\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora4.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora4.jpg?resize=320%2C223&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora4.jpg?resize=600%2C418&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora4.jpg?resize=768%2C535&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p>And then, suddenly, the aurora appears, its &#8220;wide wings of light&#8221; sweeping across the sky to widen the child&#8217;s eyes with wonder.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Seeking-Aurora-Elizabeth-Pulford/dp/1733121277/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora23.jpg?resize=680%2C453&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"453\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-73094\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora23.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, /></a></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Seeking-Aurora-Elizabeth-Pulford/dp/1733121277/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora5.jpg?resize=680%2C470&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"470\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-73085\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora5.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora24.jpg?resize=680%2C453&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"453\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-73093\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora24.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, /></a></p>\n<blockquote><p>Dancing light, glowing and glimmering,<br />\nshimmering and shining.<br />\nColored ribbons swirling and twirling,<br />\nlighting up the sky on the still, dark night.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Father and child are silent under the soft technicolor sky &#8212; an awed silence that evokes the works of the poet Diane Ackerman, who wrote long ago in her <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/02/19/diane-ackerman-the-planets-a-cosmic-pastoral/\">stunning <em>Cosmic Pastoral</em></a> of feeling &#8220;stricken by the ricochet wonder of it all: the plain everythingness of everything, in cahoots with the everythingness of everything else.&#8221;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Seeking-Aurora-Elizabeth-Pulford/dp/1733121277/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora25.jpg?resize=680%2C448&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"448\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-73092\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora25.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora25.jpg?resize=320%2C211&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora25.jpg?resize=600%2C395&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora25.jpg?resize=240%2C158&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora25.jpg?resize=768%2C506&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p>On the walk home, back to the house with the warm buttery light, the father shares everything he knows about the aurora &#8212; a secret everythingness revealed on the last page of the book, in a brief science primer of an afterword, sweetly titled &#8220;Everything Dad Knew about the Aurora.&#8221;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Seeking-Aurora-Elizabeth-Pulford/dp/1733121277/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora20.jpg?resize=680%2C458&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"458\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-73097\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora20.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora20.jpg?resize=320%2C216&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora20.jpg?resize=600%2C405&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora20.jpg?resize=240%2C162&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora20.jpg?resize=768%2C518&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p>Couple <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Seeking-Aurora-Elizabeth-Pulford/dp/1733121277/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Seeking an Aurora</em></strong></a> with the inspiring <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/10/01/what-miss-mitchell-saw/\">picture-book biography of trailblazing astronomer Maria Mitchell</a>, then revisit a literary titan&#8217;s account of the other great cosmic spectacle visible from Earth &#8212; Virginia Woolf&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/05/09/virginia-woolf-eclipse/\">arresting meditation on the total solar eclipse</a>.</p>\n<p class=\"via\"><em>Illustrations courtesy of <a nt/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora24.jpg?resize=680%2C453&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn11@2020_2/2021/04/03/04-49-44-961_de4ce7812fe568cc.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora25.jpg?resize=680%2C448&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn91@2020_2/2021/04/03/04-49-46-112_1ddb7ef9cb03ef8a.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/seekinganaurora20.jpg?resize=680%2C458&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn67@2020_3/2021/04/03/04-49-43-227_c37ddbbf99c707bc.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/Pbz95ggVo3A":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn31@2020_5/2021/04/03/04-49-44-142_3cc447080fe69b18.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617425326481},{"createdTime":"2021-04-03 12:48:46","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:48:46","title":"Secrets from the Center of the World: Poet Joy Harjo’s Reflections on Science and Meaning in Response to an Astronomer’s Otherworldly Photographs of Earth","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=73051","description":"<h3>&#8220;I can hear the sizzle of newborn stars, and know anything of meaning, of the fierce magic emerging here. I am witness to flexible eternity, the evolving past, and I know we will live forever, as dust or breath in the face of stars, in the shifting pattern of winds.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Secrets-Center-World-Sun-Tracks/dp/0816511136/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"320\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/secretsfromthecenteroftheworld_harjo_strom.jpg?fit=320%2C320&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover-landscape alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Secrets from the Center of the World: Poet Joy Harjo&#8217;s Reflections on Science and Meaning in Response to an Astronomer&#8217;s Otherworldly Photographs of Earth\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/secretsfromthecenteroftheworld_harjo_strom.jpg?w=1000&#38;ssl=1 1000w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/secretsfromthecenteroftheworld_harjo_strom.jpg?resize=320%2C320&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/secretsfromthecenteroftheworld_harjo_strom.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/secretsfromthecenteroftheworld_harjo_strom.jpg?resize=240%2C240&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/secretsfromthecenteroftheworld_harjo_strom.jpg?resize=768%2C768&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>“Place and a mind may interpenetrate till the nature of both is altered,” the trailblazing Scottish mountaineer and poet Nan Shepherd wrote into the void of self-elected obscurity decades before her work was <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/03/19/the-living-mountain-nan-shepherd/\">posthumously rediscovered</a> as a rare masterpiece of landscape poetics irradiated by the human search for meaning. A generation later, another trailblazing woman of uncommon poetic sensibility and intimate relationship to the land echoed the sentiment in her own art, into her native canyons of the American Southwest: &#8220;It&#8217;s true that landscape forms the mind. If I stand here long enough I&#8217;ll learn how to sing.&#8221;</p>\n<p>In 1989, long before she became Poet Laureate of the United States, <strong>Joy Harjo</strong> entwined visions with the astronomer and photographer <a href=\"https://www.stephenstrom.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Stephen Strom</a> in <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Secrets-Center-World-Sun-Tracks/dp/0816511136/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Secrets from the Center of the World</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/secrets-from-the-center-of-the-world/oclc/634091116&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; a  slender, splendid installment in the University of Arizona&#8217;s wonderful <em>Sun Tracks</em> series, celebrating Native American literary art long before Native representation rose to the fore of the American mainstream, long before the English language awakened to how deeply its etymological reliance on the Earth permeates words as mundane as <em>mainstream</em>.</p>\n<p>Emerging from the lovely call-and-response between Strom&#8217;s photographs and Harjo&#8217;s short lyrical reflection is a subtle meditation on the interpenetration of place and mind, of landscape and the human spirit. Contemplating the ochre canyons and the golden valleys, the pleated sierras and the billowing mudhills, the frosty branches of the winter trees and the summer-blazed strata of sandstone, she unfolds the origami of deep time into a note some ghost-mother left for her ghost-child long ago on the edge of the kitchen table, on the edge of the world, inscribed with the meaning of being human.  </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73058\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Secrets-Center-World-Sun-Tracks/dp/0816511136/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/BluffHogan.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"600\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73058\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/BluffHogan.jpg?w=600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/BluffHogan.jpg?resize=320%2C320&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/BluffHogan.jpg?resize=240%2C240&#38;ssl=1 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Abandoned hogan south of Bluff, UT</em> by <a href=\"https://www.stephenstrom.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Stephen Strom</a></figcaption></figure>\n<blockquote><p>This land is a poem of ochre and burnt sand I could never write, unless paper were the sacrament of sky, and ink the broken line of wild horses staggering the horizon several miles away. Even then, does anything written ever matter to the earth, wind, and sky?</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73052\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Secrets-Center-World-Sun-Tracks/dp/0816511136/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/BVMudhills-2.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"600\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73052\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/BVMudhills-2.jpg?w=600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/BVMudhills-2.jpg?resize=320%2C320&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/BVMudhills-2.jpg?resize=240%2C240&#38;ssl=1 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Mudhills, Beautiful Valley</em> by <a href=\"https://www.stephenstrom.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Stephen Strom</a></figcaption></figure>\n<blockquote><p>If all events are related, then what story does a volcano erupting in Hawaii, the birth of a woman&#8217;s second son near Gallup, and this shoulderbone of earth made of a mythic monster&#8217;s anger construct? Nearby a meteor crashes. Someone invents aerodynamics, makes wings. The answer is like rushing wind: simple faith.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Strom &#8212; who received his doctoral degree from Harvard, studied the formation of star and planetary systems at the National Optical Astronomy Observatory, taught astronomy in Emily Dickinson&#8217;s hometown for a decade and a half, and spent three decades photographing the Southwest &#8212; renders Earth otherworldly in his photographs, spare and solitary, edged in by invisible implied horizons, the way the desert implies life, the way poetry makes life visible. Revealing <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/02/22/mandelbrot-fractals-chaos/\">the fractal patterning of nature</a>, his subtle geometries of shape and color reach beyond the three spatial dimensions to intimate the dimension of time.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73057\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Secrets-Center-World-Sun-Tracks/dp/0816511136/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/BurnhamMudhills.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"600\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73057\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/BurnhamMudhills.jpg?w=600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/BurnhamMudhills.jpg?resize=320%2C320&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/BurnhamMudhills.jpg?resize=240%2C240&#38;ssl=1 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Near Burnham, Bisti Badlands</em> by <a href=\"https://www.stephenstrom.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Stephen Strom</a></figcaption></figure>\n<blockquote><p>These smoky bluffs are old traveling companions, making their way through millennia. Ask them if you want to know about the true meaning of history. You&#8217;ll have to offer them something more than one good story, and need to understand the patience of stones.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Harjo &#8212; a member of the Creek Nation &#8212; meets the cosmological sensibility of the photographs with a private cosmogony drawn from that ancient human impulse to locate ourselves in relation to the universe, to make meaning in the sliver of spacetime on which chance has perched us to live out our lives between the scale of protozoa and the scale of galaxies. She envelops each photograph in a short prose-poem that takes the image as its origin point of contemplation, then radiates centrifugally into a miniature universe of metaphor and meaning-making &#8212; the mark of all great poetry.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73054\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Secrets-Center-World-Sun-Tracks/dp/0816511136/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/NearRoundRock.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"600\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73054\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/NearRoundRock.jpg?w=600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/NearRoundRock.jpg?resize=320%2C320&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/NearRoundRock.jpg?resize=240%2C240&#38;ssl=1 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Desert Floor near Round Rock, AZ</em> by <a href=\"https://www.stephenstrom.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Stephen Strom</a></figcaption></figure>\n<blockquote><p>Near Round Rock is a point of balance between two red stars. Here you may enter galactic memory, disguised as a whirlpool of sand, and discover you are pure event mixed with water, occurring in time and space, as sheep, a few goats, graze, keep watch nearby.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73059\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Secrets-Center-World-Sun-Tracks/dp/0816511136/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/JunctionOverlook.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"600\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73059\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/JunctionOverlook.jpg?w=600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/JunctionOverlook.jpg?resize=320%2C320&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/JunctionOverlook.jpg?resize=240%2C240&#38;ssl=1 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Junction Overlook, Canyon de Chelly</em> by <a href=\"https://www.stephenstrom.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Stephen Strom</a></figcaption></figure>\n<blockquote><p>My house is the red earth; it could be the center of the world. I’ve heard New York, Paris, or Tokyo called the center of the world, but I say it is magnificently humble. You could drive by and miss it. Radio waves can obscure it. Words cannot construct it, for there are some sounds left to sacred wordless form. For instance, that fool crow, picking through trash near the corral, understands the center of the world as greasy strips of fat. Just ask him. He doesn’t have to say that the earth has turned scarlet through fierce belief, after centuries of heartbreak and laughter &#8212; he perches on the blue bowl of the sky, and laughs.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73061\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Secrets-Center-World-Sun-Tracks/dp/0816511136/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/BluffOverlookEvening.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"600\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73061\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/BluffOverlookEvening.jpg?w=600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/BluffOverlookEvening.jpg?resize=320%2C320&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/BluffOverlookEvening.jpg?resize=240%2C240&#38;ssl=1 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Overlook, evening, Bluff, UT</em> by <a href=\"https://www.stephenstrom.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Stephen Strom</a></figcaption></figure>\n<blockquote><p>This earth has dreamed me to stand on the rise of this highway, to admire who she has become.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73060\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Secrets-Center-World-Sun-Tracks/dp/0816511136/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/DFloorShiprock.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"600\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73060\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/DFloorShiprock.jpg?w=600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/DFloorShiprock.jpg?resize=320%2C320&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/DFloorShiprock.jpg?resize=240%2C240&#38;ssl=1 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Desert floor near Shiprock, NM</em> by <a href=\"https://www.stephenstrom.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Stephen Strom</a></figcaption></figure>\n<blockquote><p>My cheek is flat against memory described by stone and lichen. The center of the world is within reach. It is as familiar as your name, as strange as monsters in your sleep.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Harjo looks at the Moon and sees &#8220;an ancient mountain lion who shifts his bones on a starry branch,&#8221; looks at the branches of the tamaracks and sees crows &#8220;leaning over the edge of the world, tasting the wind blown up from a pool of newly born planets,&#8221; looks at the land and sees its elemental poetry, sees how it humbles her own art, her own existence, every human existence and all of our art.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73056\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Secrets-Center-World-Sun-Tracks/dp/0816511136/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/GanadotoChinleWinter.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"600\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73056\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/GanadotoChinleWinter.jpg?w=600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/GanadotoChinleWinter.jpg?resize=320%2C320&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/GanadotoChinleWinter.jpg?resize=240%2C240&#38;ssl=1 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>East of Nazlini, going up toward Fort Defiance Plateau, winter</em> by <a href=\"https://www.stephenstrom.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Stephen Strom</a></figcaption></figure>\n<blockquote><p>In winter it is easier to see what my death might look like, over there, disappearing into the misty, spotted rocks.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73053\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Secrets-Center-World-Sun-Tracks/dp/0816511136/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/NazliniMudhills.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"600\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73053\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/NazliniMudhills.jpg?w=600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/NazliniMudhills.jpg?resize=240%2C240&#38;ssl=1 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Mudhills near Nazlini</em> by <a href=\"https://www.stephenstrom.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Stephen Strom</a></figcaption></figure>\n<blockquote><p>I can hear the sizzle of newborn stars, and know anything of meaning, of the fierce magic emerging here. I am witness to flexible eternity, the evolving past, and I know we will live forever, as dust or breath in the face of stars, in the shifting pattern of winds.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Complement <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Secrets-Center-World-Sun-Tracks/dp/0816511136/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Secrets from the Center of the World</em></strong></a> with poet Mark Strand&#8217;s kindred collaboration with painter Wendy Mark around the landscape of the sky, <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/03/02/89-clouds-mark-strand-wendy-mark/\"><em>89 Clouds</em></a>, then revisit painter, poet, and philosopher Etel Adnan&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/02/06/etel-adnan-journey-to-mount-tamalpais/\"><em>Journey to Mount Tamalpais</em></a> &#8212; her stunning landscape-lensed meditation on time, self, impermanence, and transcendence. </p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going.
