12:48:46","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:48:46","title":"Gertrude Stein on Writing and Belonging","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=73111","description":"<h3>&#8220;Everybody who writes is interested in living inside themselves to tell what is inside themselves.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Paris-France-Gertrude-Stein/dp/0871403749/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"480\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/gertrudestein_parisfrance.jpg?fit=320%2C480&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Gertrude Stein on Writing and Belonging\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/gertrudestein_parisfrance.jpg?w=907&#38;ssl=1 907w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/gertrudestein_parisfrance.jpg?resize=320%2C480&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/gertrudestein_parisfrance.jpg?resize=600%2C900&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/gertrudestein_parisfrance.jpg?resize=240%2C360&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/gertrudestein_parisfrance.jpg?resize=768%2C1152&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>“You only are free when you realize you belong no place &#8212; you belong every place &#8212; no place at all,” Maya Angelou told Bill Moyers in their <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/06/14/maya-angelou-bill-moyers-1973/\">fantastic forgotten conversation about freedom</a>. Beneath the surface of this paradoxical sentiment is a kind of koan, simple yet profound, replete with layered truth for those of us living expatriated lives &#8212; expatriated from a place or a culture, in space or in time. </p>\n<p>Two generations before Angelou, <strong>Gertrude Stein</strong> (February 3, 1874&#8211;July 27, 1946), living out <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/08/28/maira-kalman-the-autobiography-of-alice-b-toklas/\">her great love story</a> as an American expatriate in Paris, addressed this paradox with uncommon insight and her own characteristic koan-like style in a passage from her 1940 novel <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Paris-France-Gertrude-Stein/dp/0871403749/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Paris France</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/paris-france/oclc/999861268&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>). </p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/08/28/maira-kalman-the-autobiography-of-alice-b-toklas/\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/MairaKalman_SteinToklas2.jpg\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Gertrude Stein by artist Maira Kalman from her <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/08/28/maira-kalman-the-autobiography-of-alice-b-toklas/\">superb illustrated edition</a> of Stein&#8217;s <em>The Autobiography of Alice B. Toklas</em>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Stein &#8212; Jewish and gay, writing while the world was coming undone by warring nationalisms and gas chambers disbelonging human beings from life itself &#8212; observes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Everybody, that is, everybody who writes is interested in living inside themselves to tell what is inside themselves. That is why writers have to have two countries, the one where they belong and the one in which they live really. The second one is romantic, it is separate from themselves, it is not real but it is really there.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Stein notes that the Victorians found their romantic home in Italy, Americans found theirs in Spain in the first half of the nineteenth century and in England in the second, and her own generation found it in Paris. Prefiguring Angelou&#8217;s sentiment, she adds:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Of course sometimes people discover their own country as if it were the other&#8230; but in general that other country that you need to be free is in the other country not the country where you really belong.</p></blockquote>\n<p>I read this and think of Leonard Cohen&#8217;s lovely notion of poetry as <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/03/01/leonard-cohen-death-of-a-ladys-man-words/\">&#8220;the Constitution of the inner country.&#8221;</a> For me, living an unbelonging life in a country other than the one in which I was born and raised, <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/tag/poetry/\">poetry</a> has been an increasingly vital portal to that inner landscape of freedom that Stein contours &#8212; a way of tending to and befriending the interior wilderness from which all creative work springs and which remains a sovereign territory of psychogeography, wherever one&#8217;s body may be located and whatever artificial borders may be drawn around it by outside observers. </p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/08/28/maira-kalman-the-autobiography-of-alice-b-toklas/\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/MairaKalman_SteinToklas9.jpg\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Maira Kalman from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/08/28/maira-kalman-the-autobiography-of-alice-b-toklas/\"><em>The Autobiography of Alice B. Toklas</em></a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Complement with poet and philosopher David Whyte on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/06/29/david-whyte-belonging/\">how to be at home in yourself</a> and Toni Morrison on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/08/06/toni-mirrison-borders-home/\">borders and belonging</a>, then revisit Maria Kalman&#8217;s magnificent <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/08/28/maira-kalman-the-autobiography-of-alice-b-toklas/\">illustrated love letter to Gertrude and Alice&#8217;s love</a>. </p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your life more livable in any way, please consider aiding its sustenance with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/donate/\">donation</a>.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p>Brain Pickings has a free weekly newsletter. It comes out on Sundays and offers the week’s most inspiring reading. Here’s <a href=\"https://mailchi.mp/brainpickings/janna-levin-rebecca-elson-anne-lamott-james-gleick\">what to expect</a>. Like? <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/newsletter/\">Sign up.</a></p><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/V8hjkjKsmJo\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 31 Mar 2021 01:27:17 +0000","feedId":17,"bgimg":"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/gertrudestein_parisfrance.jpg?fit=320%2C480&ssl=1","linkMd5":"10a9fa4a2b97b1738a0c8b66c834480f","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn33@2020_3/2021/04/03/04-49-31-330_e43654b63342c4a9.webp","destWidth":320,"destHeight":480,"sourceBytes":16722,"destBytes":16722,"author":"Maria Popova","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/gertrudestein_parisfrance.jpg?fit=320%2C480&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn33@2020_3/2021/04/03/04-49-31-330_e43654b63342c4a9.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/MairaKalman_SteinToklas2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn39@2020_1/2021/04/03/04-49-45-307_c68fcd63c33693d5.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/MairaKalman_SteinToklas9.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn3@2020_2/2021/04/03/04-49-42-255_54ebbfc98166cffa.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/V8hjkjKsmJo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn39@2020_4/2021/04/03/04-49-42-802_0cbaaf9e4005adb4.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617425326498},{"createdTime":"2021-04-03 12:48:46","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:48:46","title":"Of Trees, Tenderness, and the Moon: Hasui Kawase’s Stunning Japanese Woodblock Prints from the 1920s-1950s","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=73023","description":"<h3>Sylvan sublimity between the heavens and the deep blue sea.</h3>\n<hr>\n<p>&#8220;After you have exhausted what there is in business, politics, conviviality, love, and so on &#8212; have found that none of these finally satisfy, or permanently wear &#8212; what remains?&#8221; the aging Walt Whitman asked in his diary as he <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/12/20/walt-whitman-specimen-days-meaning-of-life/\">contemplated what makes life worth living</a> while recovering from a paralytic stroke, then answered: &#8220;Nature remains&#8230; the trees, fields, the changes of seasons &#8212; the sun by day and the stars of heaven by night.&#8221;</p>\n<p>A century after Whitman&#8217;s birth, on the other side of a globe newly disillusioned with its own humanity after the First World War, a young Japanese man was embarking on a life of celebrating the inexhaustible consolations of nature in uncommonly poetic visual art. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73032\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase2.jpg?resize=680%2C1025&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1025\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73032\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase2.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase2.jpg?resize=320%2C482&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase2.jpg?resize=600%2C904&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase2.jpg?resize=240%2C362&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase2.jpg?resize=768%2C1157&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase2.jpg?resize=1019%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1019w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Moon at Magome</em>, 1930. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/moon-at-magome-by-hasui-kawase-1930_print?sku=s6-19564911p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Born into a Tokyo family of rope and thread merchants, <strong>Hasui Kawase</strong> (May 18, 1883&#8211;November 7, 1957) grew up dreaming of becoming an artist. His parents pressed him to continue in their path, but he persisted in following his own, drawing quiet inspiration from the example of his maternal uncle &#8212; the creator of the first manga magazine. </p>\n<p>He did take over the family business, but he was moonlighting in art while running it &#8212; sketching from nature, copying one master&#8217;s woodblock prints, learning brush painting from another. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73034\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/sunset-at-ichinokura-by-hasui-kawase-1928_print?sku=s6-19565000p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase5.jpg?resize=680%2C454&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"454\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73034\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase5.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase5.jpg?resize=320%2C214&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase5.jpg?resize=600%2C401&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase5.jpg?resize=240%2C160&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase5.jpg?resize=768%2C513&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Sunset at Ichinokura</em>, 1928. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/sunset-at-ichinokura-by-hasui-kawase-1928_print?sku=s6-19565000p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>When the business went bankrupt in the early twentieth century, the twenty-six-year-old Kawase devoted himself wholly to art, applying to apprentice with one of the great masters of transitional Japanese woodblock printing. The master rejected him, encouraging him to broaden his sensibility and to develop his style by studying Western painting first. The young man obliged. </p>\n<p>Two years later, he applied again. </p>\n<p>The master accepted him, conferring upon him the lyrical name Hasui &#8212; an ideogram of his family name fused with the name of his boyhood school, most closely translated translated as &#8220;water springing from the source.&#8221;</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73026\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/spring-moon-at-ninomiya-beach-by-hasui-kawase-1931_print?sku=s6-19564891p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?resize=680%2C1014&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1014\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73026\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?resize=320%2C477&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?resize=600%2C895&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?resize=240%2C358&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?resize=768%2C1146&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?resize=1030%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1030w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Spring Moon at Ninomiya Beach</em>, 1931. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/spring-moon-at-ninomiya-beach-by-hasui-kawase-1931_print?sku=s6-19564891p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Hasui was thirty-five &#8212; the age Whitman was when he staggered the world with his <em>Leaves of Grass</em> &#8212; when he made his artistic debut with a series of experimental woodblock prints, depicting the mostly empty streets of Tokyo and the unpeopled landscapes of the countryside. </p>\n<p>As he began his next series, nature and night beckoned to him more and more . </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73029\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/moon-over-akebi-bridge-by-hasui-kawase-1935_print?sku=s6-19565084p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase9.jpg?resize=680%2C1056&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1056\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73029\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase9.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase9.jpg?resize=320%2C497&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase9.jpg?resize=600%2C932&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase9.jpg?resize=240%2C373&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase9.jpg?resize=768%2C1193&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase9.jpg?resize=989%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 989w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Moon Over Akebi Bridge</em>, 1935. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/moon-over-akebi-bridge-by-hasui-kawase-1935_print?sku=s6-19565084p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>And then, on an otherwise ordinary Saturday the autumn after his fortieth birthday, the convergence boundary between two tectonic plates deep in the body of the Earth ruptured, unleashing the Great Kantō earthquake of 1923. It leveled his workshop, destroying the finished woodblocks and fomenting in him an even more intimate sense of the sublimity of nature. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73028\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/autumn-rainbow-at-hatta-kaga-by-hasui-kawase-1924_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_rainbow.jpg?resize=680%2C453&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"453\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73028\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_rainbow.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_rainbow.jpg?resize=320%2C213&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_rainbow.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_rainbow.jpg?resize=240%2C160&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_rainbow.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Autumn Rainbow at Hatta, Kaga</em>, 1924. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/autumn-rainbow-at-hatta-kaga-by-hasui-kawase-1924_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Over the next thirty-five years, Hasui became a master of <em>shin hanga</em> &#8212; the &#8220;new prints&#8221; movement fusing traditional Japanese art, <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/05/28/in-praise-of-shadows-tanizaki/\">the art of shadows</a>, with the Western aesthetics of light and <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/01/02/perspective/\">the European novelty of perspective</a>. He went on to create several hundred consummate woodblock prints, watercolors, oil paintings, and hanging scrolls, animated by a tender reverence for the beauty and majesty of nature. One hundred of them are collected in the lavish annotated volume <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Visions-Japan-Kawase-Hasuis-Masterpieces-dp-9074822681/dp/9074822681/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Visions of Japan: Kawase Hasui&#8217;s Masterpieces</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/visions-of-japan-kawase-hasuis-masterpieces/oclc/899048836&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>).</p>\n<p>Hasui captured the enchantment of snowfall with especial loveliness, his intricate lines challenging the artisans he employed in carving his woodblock designs to rise to new levels of craftsmanship.  </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73025\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/snow-on-lake-by-hasui-kawase-1922_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_snow.jpg?resize=680%2C904&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"904\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73025\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_snow.jpg?w=1000&#38;ssl=1 1000w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_snow.jpg?resize=320%2C425&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_snow.jpg?resize=600%2C797&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_snow.jpg?resize=240%2C319&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_snow.jpg?resize=768%2C1021&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Snow on Lake</em>, 1922. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/snow-on-lake-by-hasui-kawase-1922_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>But among all of nature&#8217;s beauties, nothing inspired him more than trees &#8212; those eternal muses of <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/07/10/trees-ted-ed/\">scientists</a>, <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/07/14/william-blake-john-trusler-letter/\">artists</a>, <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/09/11/martin-buber-tree/\">philosophers</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/09/23/amanda-palmer-mary-oliver-when-i-am-among-the-trees/\">poets</a> alike &#8212; and what <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/06/05/ralph-waldo-emerson-margaret-fuller-letters-figuring/\">Margaret Fuller</a> so unforgettably called &#8220;that best fact, the Moon.&#8221;</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73031\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/winter-moon-at-toyamagahara-by-hasui-kawase-1931_print?sku=s6-19564919p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase3.jpg?resize=680%2C1005&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1005\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73031\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase3.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase3.jpg?resize=320%2C473&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase3.jpg?resize=600%2C887&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase3.jpg?resize=240%2C355&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase3.jpg?resize=768%2C1135&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase3.jpg?resize=1039%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1039w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Winter Moon at Toyamagahara</em>, 1931. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/winter-moon-at-toyamagahara-by-hasui-kawase-1931_print?sku=s6-19564919p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73030\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/spring-night-at-inokashira-by-hasui-kawase-1931_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase8.jpg?resize=680%2C1005&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1005\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73030\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase8.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase8.jpg?resize=320%2C473&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase8.jpg?resize=600%2C887&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase8.jpg?resize=240%2C355&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase8.jpg?resize=768%2C1135&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase8.jpg?resize=1039%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1039w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Spring Night at Inokashira</em>, 1931. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/spring-night-at-inokashira-by-hasui-kawase-1931_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In landscape after landscape, the majestic silhouettes of the <em>matsu</em> (Japan&#8217;s iconic pine trees, symbols of fortitude and courage) and the <em>sugi</em> (the enormous old-growth cedars, symbols of power and longevity) reach into the noctrune toward the crescent and lean into the gloaming hour, backlit by the full Moon.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73035\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/crescent-moon-and-tea-houses-kanazawa-by-hasui-kawase-1920s_print?sku=s6-19564934p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase4.jpg?resize=680%2C1002&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1002\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73035\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase4.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase4.jpg?resize=320%2C471&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase4.jpg?resize=600%2C884&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase4.jpg?resize=240%2C354&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase4.jpg?resize=768%2C1132&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase4.jpg?resize=1043%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1043w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Crescent Moon and Tea Houses, Kanazawa</em>, 1920s. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/crescent-moon-and-tea-houses-kanazawa-by-hasui-kawase-1920s_print?sku=s6-19564934p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73036\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/hikawa-park-in-omiya-by-hasui-kawase-1930_print?sku=s6-19565055p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase7.jpg?resize=680%2C1020&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1020\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73036\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase7.jpg?w=1000&#38;ssl=1 1000w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase7.jpg?resize=320%2C480&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase7.jpg?resize=600%2C900&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase7.jpg?resize=240%2C360&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase7.jpg?resize=768%2C1152&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Hikawa Park in Omiya</em>, 1930. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/hikawa-park-in-omiya-by-hasui-kawase-1930_print?sku=s6-19565055p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73033\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/moon-over-arakawa-river-by-hasui-kawase-1929_print?sku=s6-19565025p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase6.jpg?resize=680%2C1003&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1003\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73033\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase6.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase6.jpg?resize=320%2C472&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase6.jpg?resize=600%2C885&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase6.jpg?resize=240%2C354&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase6.jpg?resize=768%2C1133&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase6.jpg?resize=1041%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1041w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Moon over Arakawa River</em>, 1929. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/moon-over-arakawa-river-by-hasui-kawase-1929_print?sku=s6-19565025p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In the final year of his life, the Japanese government classified Hasui as a Living National Treasure. Comparable to the American National Medal of Arts and Humanities, Japan&#8217;s highest civilian honor is bestowed upon those whose life&#8217;s work renders them, in what may be the most poetic government certification in any language, &#8220;Preservers of Important Intangible Cultural Properties.&#8221;</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73027\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/kankai-pavilion-at-wakaura-beach-by-hasui-kawase-1950_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_11.jpg?resize=680%2C455&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"455\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73027\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_11.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_11.jpg?resize=320%2C214&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_11.jpg?resize=600%2C402&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_11.jpg?resize=240%2C161&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_11.jpg?resize=768%2C514&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Kankai Pavilion at Wakaura Beach</em>, 1950. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/kankai-pavilion-at-wakaura-beach-by-hasui-kawase-1950_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Complement with Japanese-American artist Chiura Obata&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/03/23/chiura-obata-yosemite/\">stunning paintings of Yosemite</a> from the same era, then revisit a <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/08/06/trees-at-night-art-young/\">very different take on tree silhouettes</a> from Hasui&#8217;s American contemporary Art Young. </p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. hasuikawase7.jpg?resize=680%2C1020&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn20@2020_3/2021/04/03/04-49-45-195_fffd0b5547169bde.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase6.jpg?resize=680%2C1003&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn59@2020_3/2021/04/03/04-49-46-727_d2f4869c763ba498.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase_11.jpg?resize=680%2C455&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn47@2020_2/2021/04/03/04-49-46-591_068bb8b157c6ab56.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/axIMa2B7YBE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn88@2020_4/2021/04/03/04-49-46-082_adfff1daf197d475.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617425326522},{"createdTime":"2021-04-03 12:48:46","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:48:46","title":"Alan Watts on Love, the Meaning of Freedom, and the Only Real Antidote to Fear","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=72952","description":"<h3>&#8220;You cannot think simultaneously about listening to the waves and whether you are enjoying listening to the waves.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/The-Wisdom-Insecurity-Message-Anxiety/dp/0307741206/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"494\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/alanwatts_thewisdomofinsecurity.jpg?fit=320%2C494&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Alan Watts on Love, the Meaning of Freedom, and the Only Real Antidote to Fear\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/alanwatts_thewisdomofinsecurity.jpg?w=1556&#38;ssl=1 1556w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/alanwatts_thewisdomofinsecurity.jpg?resize=320%2C494&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/alanwatts_thewisdomofinsecurity.jpg?resize=600%2C925&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/alanwatts_thewisdomofinsecurity.jpg?resize=240%2C370&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/alanwatts_thewisdomofinsecurity.jpg?resize=768%2C1185&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/alanwatts_thewisdomofinsecurity.jpg?resize=996%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 996w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/alanwatts_thewisdomofinsecurity.jpg?resize=1328%2C2048&#38;ssl=1 1328w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>“Fearlessness is what love seeks,&#8221; Hannah Arendt wrote in her <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/02/25/love-and-saint-augustine-hannah-arendt/\">superb 1929 meditation on love and how to live with the fundamental fear of loss</a>. &#8220;Such fearlessness exists only in the complete calm that can no longer be shaken by events expected of the future&#8230; Hence the only valid tense is the present, the Now.” </p>\n<p>Half a century before her, Leo Tolstoy &#8212; who befriended a Buddhist monk late in life and became deeply influenced by Buddhist philosophy &#8212; echoed these ancient truths as he contemplated <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/09/09/leo-tolstoy-on-love/\">the paradoxical nature of love</a>: “Future love does not exist. Love is a present activity only.&#8221;</p>\n<p>That in love and in life, freedom from fear &#8212; like all species of freedom &#8212; is only possible within the present moment has long been a core teaching of the most ancient Eastern spiritual and philosophical traditions. It is one of the most elemental truths of existence, and one of those most difficult to put into practice as we move through our daily human lives, so habitually inclined toward the next moment and the mentally constructed universe of expected events &#8212; the parallel universe where anxiety dwells, where hope and fear for what might be eclipse what is, and where we cease to be free because we are no longer in the direct light of reality.</p>\n<p>The relationship between freedom, fear, and love is what <strong>Alan Watts</strong> (January 6, 1915&#8211;November 16, 1973) explores in one of the most insightful chapters of <a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/The-Wisdom-Insecurity-Message-Anxiety/dp/0307741206/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>The Wisdom of Insecurity: A Message for an Age of Anxiety</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"http://www.worldcat.org/title/wisdom-of-insecurity-a-message-for-an-age-of-anxiety/oclc/662402941&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; his altogether revelatory 1951 classic, which introduced Eastern philosophy to the West with its lucid and luminous case for <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/01/06/alan-watts-wisdom-of-insecurity-1/\">how to live with presence</a>. </p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/The-Wisdom-Insecurity-Message-Anxiety/dp/0307741206/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/alanwatts.jpg?w=680&#038;ssl=1\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Alan Watts, early 1970s (Image courtesy of Everett Collection)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Drawing on his <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/11/01/alan-watts-wisdom-of-insecurity-3/\">admonition against the dangers of the divided mind</a> &#8212; the mindset that divides us into interior self-awareness and external reality, into ego and universe, which is the mindset the whole of Western culture has instilled in us &#8212; he writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The meaning of freedom can never be grasped by the divided mind. If I feel separate from my experience, and from the world, freedom will seem to be the extent to which I can push the world around, and fate the extent to which the world pushes me around. But to the whole mind there is no contrast of “I” and the world. There is just one process acting, and it does everything that happens. It raises my little finger and it creates earthquakes. Or, if you want to put it that way, I raise my little finger and also make earthquakes. No one fates and no one is being fated.</p></blockquote>\n<p>This model of freedom is orthogonal to our conditioned view that freedom is a matter of bending external reality to our will by the power of our choices &#8212; controlling what remains of nature once the &#8220;I&#8221; is separated out. Watts draws a subtle, crucial distinction between freedom and choice: </p>\n<blockquote><p>What we ordinarily mean by choice is not freedom. Choices are usually decisions motivated by pleasure and pain, and the divided mind acts with the sole purpose of getting “I” into pleasure and out of pain. But the best pleasures are those for which we do not plan, and the worst part of pain is expecting it and trying to get away from it when it has come. You cannot plan to be happy. You can plan to exist, but in themselves existence and non-existence are neither pleasurable nor painful.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72735\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-thomas-wrights-an-original-theory-or-new-hypothesis-of-the-universe-17504457506_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?resize=680%2C753&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"753\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72735\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?resize=240%2C266&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?resize=320%2C354&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?resize=768%2C850&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?resize=600%2C664&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Thomas Wright from his <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/02/16/thomas-wright-original-theory/\"><em>Original Theory or New Hypothesis of the Universe</em></a>, 1750. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-thomas-wrights-an-original-theory-or-new-hypothesis-of-the-universe-17504457506_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a> and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a face mask</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Stripped of the paraphernalia of circumstance and interpretation, our internal experience of being unfree stems from attempting impossible things &#8212; things that resist reality and refuse to accept the present moment on its own terms. Watts writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The sense of not being free comes from trying to do things which are impossible and even meaningless. You are not “free” to draw a square circle, to live without a head, or to stop certain reflex actions. These are not obstacles to freedom; they are the conditions of freedom. I am not free to draw a circle if perchance it should turn out to be a square circle. I am not, thank heaven, free to walk out of doors and leave my head at home. Likewise I am not free to live in any moment but this one, or to separate myself from my feelings.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Without the motive forces of pleasure and pain, it might at first appear paradoxical to make any decisions at all &#8212; a contradiction that makes it impossible to choose between options as we navigate even the most basic realities of life: Why choose to take the umbrella into the downpour, why choose to eat this piece of mango and not this piece of cardboard? But Watts observes that the only real contradiction is of our own making as we cede the present to an imagined future. More than half a century before psychologists came to study <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/06/18/daniel-gilbert-happiness-future-self/\">how your present self is sabotaging your future happiness</a>, Watts offers the personal counterpart to Albert Camus&#8217;s astute political observation that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/06/17/albert-camus-the-rebel/\">&#8220;real generosity toward the future lies in giving all to the present,&#8221;</a> and writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>I fall straight into contradiction when I try to act and decide in order to be happy, when I make “being pleased” my future goal. For the more my actions are directed towards future pleasures, the more I am incapable of enjoying any pleasures at all. For all pleasures are present, and nothing save complete awareness of the present can even begin to guarantee future happiness.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>You can only live in one moment at a time, and you cannot think simultaneously about listening to the waves and whether you are enjoying listening to the waves. Contradictions of this kind are the only real types of action without freedom.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_64211\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/i-musing-late-in-the-autumn-day_framed-print?sku=s6-8967581p21a12v52a13v54?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass25.jpg?resize=680%2C851&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"851\" class=\"size-full wp-image-64211\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass25.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass25.jpg?resize=240%2C300&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass25.jpg?resize=320%2C401&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass25.jpg?resize=768%2C961&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass25.jpg?resize=600%2C751&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Margaret C. Cook from a <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/04/11/leaves-of-grass-margaret-cook/\">rare 1913 edition</a> of Walt Whitman&#8217;s <em>Leaves of Grass</em>. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/i-musing-late-in-the-autumn-day_framed-print?sku=s6-8967581p21a12v52a13v54?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Only with such a recalibration of our reflexive view of freedom does James Baldwin&#8217;s insistence that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/05/09/james-baldwin-freedom/\">&#8220;people are as free as they want to be&#8221;</a> begin to unfold its layered meaning like a Zen koan, to be turned over in the mind until the deceptively simple shape unfolds its origami-folded scroll of deep truth. </p>\n<p>In what may be the most elegant refutation of the particular strain of hubris that embraces determinism in order to wring from it the self-permission for living with delirious freedom from responsibility, Watts writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>There is another theory of determinism which states that all our actions are motivated by “unconscious mental mechanisms,” and that for this reason even the most spontaneous decisions are not free. This is but another example of split-mindedness, for what is the difference between “me” and “mental mechanisms” whether conscious or unconscious? Who is being moved by these processes? The notion that anyone is being motivated comes from the persisting illusion of “I.” The real man<a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/10/17/ursula-k-le-guin-gender/\">*</a>, the organism-in-relation-to-the-universe, <em>is</em> this unconscious motivation. And because he <em>is</em> it, he is not being moved <em>by</em> it.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>Events look inevitable in retrospect because when they have happened, nothing can change them. Yet the fact that I can make safe bets could prove equally well that events are not <em>determined</em> but <em>consistent</em>. In other words, the universal process acts freely and spontaneously at every moment, but tends to throw out events in regular, and so predictable, sequences.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Only by such a misapprehension of freedom, Watts observes, do we ever feel unfree: When we enter a state that causes us psychological pain, our immediate impulse is to get the &#8220;I&#8221; out of the pain, which is invariably a resistance to the present moment as it is; because we cannot will a different psychological state, we reach for an easy escape: a drink, a drug, a compulsive scroll through an Instagram feed. All the ways in which we try to abate our feelings of abject loneliness and boredom and inadequacy by escaping from the present moment where they unfold are motivated by the fear that those intolerable feelings will subsume us. And yet the instant we become motivated by fear, we become unfree &#8212; we are prisoners of fear. We are only free within the bounds of the present moment, with all of its disquieting feelings, because only in that moment can they dissipate into the totality of integrated reality, leaving no divide between us as feelers and the feelings being felt, and therefore no painful contrast between preferred state and actual state. Watts writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>So long as the mind believes in the possibility of escape from what it is at this moment, there can be no freedom.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>It <em>sounds</em> as if it were the most abject fatalism to have to admit that I am what I am, and that no escape or division is possible. It seems that if I <em>am</em> afraid, then I am “stuck” with fear. But in fact I am chained to the fear only so long as I am trying to get away from it. On the other hand, when I do not try to get away I discover that there is nothing “stuck” or fixed about the reality of the moment. When I am aware of this feeling without naming it, without calling it “fear,” “bad,” “negative,” etc., it changes instantly into something else, and life moves freely ahead. The feeling no longer perpetuates itself by creating the feeler behind it.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72737\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-thomas-wrights-an-original-theory-or-new-hypothesis-of-the-universe-1750_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?resize=680%2C977&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"977\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72737\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?resize=240%2C345&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?resize=320%2C460&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?resize=768%2C1103&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?resize=600%2C862&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Thomas Wright from his <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/02/16/thomas-wright-original-theory/\"><em>Original Theory or New Hypothesis of the Universe</em></a>, 1750. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-thomas-wrights-an-original-theory-or-new-hypothesis-of-the-universe-1750_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a> and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a face mask</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>To dissolve into this total reality of the moment is the crucible of freedom, which is in turn the crucible of love. In consonance with Toni Morrison&#8217;s insistence that the deepest measure of freedom is <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/09/10/toni-morrison-beloved-freedom/\">loving anything and anyone you choose to love</a> and with that classic, exquisite Adrienne Rich sonnet line &#8212; <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2012/12/14/adrienne-rich-on-love-loss-happiness-creativity/\">&#8220;no one’s fated or doomed to love anyone&#8221;</a> &#8212; Watts considers the ultimate reward of this undivided mind:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The further truth that the undivided mind is aware of experience as a unity, of the world as itself, and that the whole nature of mind and awareness is to be one with what it knows, suggests a state that would usually be called love&#8230; Love is the organizing and unifying principle which makes the world a <em>uni</em>verse and the disintegrated mass a community. It is the very essence and character of mind, and becomes manifest in action when the mind is whole&#8230; This, rather than any mere emotion, is the power and principle of free action.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Complement this fragment of the timelessly rewarding <a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/The-Wisdom-Insecurity-Message-Anxiety/dp/0307741206/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>The Wisdom of Insecurity</em></strong></a> with Watts on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/11/06/alan-watts-swimming-headless/\">learning not to think in terms of gain and loss</a> and <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/03/25/sense-of-nonsense-alan-watts-tao-of-philosophy/\">finding meaning by accepting the meaninglessness of life</a>, then revisit Seneca on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/08/27/seneca-anxiety/\">the antidote to anxiety</a> and astronomer Rebecca Elson&#8217;s almost unbearably beautiful poem <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/04/10/antidotes-to-fear-of-death-rebecca-elson/\">&#8220;Antidotes to Fear of Death.&#8221;</a></p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your life more livable in any way, please consider aiding its sustenance with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/donate/\">donation</a>.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p>Brain Pickings has a free weekly newsletter. It comes out on Sundays and offers the week’s most inspiring reading. Here’s <a href=\"https://mailchi.mp/brainpickings/janna-levin-rebecca-elson-anne-lamott-james-gleick\">what to expect</a>. Like? <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/newsletter/\">Sign up.</a></p><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/FCadxUsqC7E\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 16 Mar 2021 16:14:40 +0000","feedId":17,"bgimg":"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/alanwatts_thewisdomofinsecurity.jpg?fit=320%2C494&ssl=1","linkMd5":"01d1fea77c3fb41bfdb6c20a1b14147a","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn11@2020_6/2021/04/03/04-49-03-111_1301b4e097d3af47.webp","destWidth":320,"destHeight":494,"sourceBytes":19394,"destBytes":19394,"author":"Maria Popova","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/alanwatts_thewisdomofinsecurity.jpg?fit=320%2C494&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn11@2020_6/2021/04/03/04-49-03-111_1301b4e097d3af47.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/alanwatts.jpg?w=680&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn82@2020_3/2021/04/03/04-49-42-268_577be82fd3ba9803.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?resize=680%2C753&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn91@2020_6/2021/04/03/04-49-44-738_ba379a95ab5527d4.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass25.jpg?resize=680%2C851&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn75@2020_1/2021/04/03/04-49-46-831_470ab3c4a38a2d15.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?resize=680%2C977&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn3@2020_6/2021/04/03/04-49-43-718_f7830f8bd1d0bd46.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/FCadxUsqC7E":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn15@2020_5/2021/04/03/04-49-42-231_fad2ebcda8d64bfc.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617425326523},{"createdTime":"2021-04-03 12:48:46","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:48:46","title":"Wintering: Resilience, the Wisdom of Sadness, and How the Science of Trees Illuminates the Art of Self-Renewal Through Difficult Times","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=72863","description":"<h3>&#8220;Wintering&#8230; is the courage to stare down the worst parts of our experience and to commit to healing them the best we can. Wintering is a moment of intuition, our true needs felt keenly as a knife.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Wintering-Power-Retreat-Difficult-Times/dp/0593189485/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"483\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/wintering_katherinemay.jpg?fit=320%2C483&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Wintering: Resilience, the Wisdom of Sadness, and How the Science of Trees Illuminates the Art of Self-Renewal Through Difficult Times\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/wintering_katherinemay.jpg?w=1688&#38;ssl=1 1688w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/wintering_katherinemay.jpg?resize=240%2C363&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/wintering_katherinemay.jpg?resize=320%2C483&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/wintering_katherinemay.jpg?resize=768%2C1160&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/wintering_katherinemay.jpg?resize=600%2C906&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/wintering_katherinemay.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>Rilke reverenced winter as <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/01/12/rilke-letters-to-a-young-woman-winter/\">the season for tending to the inner garden of the soul</a>: &#8220;Suddenly to be healed again and aware that the very ground of my being &#8212; my mind and spirit &#8212; was given time and space in which to go on growing,&#8221; he wrote to a grief-stricken young woman who had reached out to him for consolation. “In the depths of winter, I finally learned that within me there lay an invincible summer,” Albert Camus wrote a generation later in his stunning essays about travel, which are really meditations on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/12/28/albert-camus-almond-trees-character/\">homecoming to our strength</a>. Camus was soon to become the second-youngest Nobel laureate of all time and soon to die in a car crash with an unused train ticket to the same destination in his pocket. We are not invincible. But in how we garden the winters of the soul, we find the summer of our strength and the bloom of our fragile aliveness.</p>\n<p>That is what <strong>Katherine May</strong> explores in <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Wintering-Power-Retreat-Difficult-Times/dp/0593189485/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_&#34;blank&#34;\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Wintering: The Power of Rest and Retreat in Difficult Times</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/wintering-the-power-of-rest-and-retreat-in-difficult-times/oclc/1231994370&#38;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; a gorgeous book, a generous book, a layered book of uncommon sensitivity and substance, drawn from May&#8217;s own experience of living through a deep and disquieting winter of life. She writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>[Since childhood] we are taught to ignore sadness, to stuff it down into our satchels and pretend it isn’t there. As adults, we often have to learn to hear the clarity of its call. That is wintering. It is the active acceptance of sadness. It is the practice of allowing ourselves to feel it as a need. It is the courage to stare down the worst parts of our experience and to commit to healing them the best we can. Wintering is a moment of intuition, our true needs felt keenly as a knife.</p></blockquote>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/10/29/the-shadow-elephant/\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/shadowelepant10.jpg\"></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Valerio Vidali from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/10/29/the-shadow-elephant/\"><em>The Shadow Elephant</em></a> by Nadine Robert &#8212; a subtle children&#8217;s book about honoring sadness.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Like happiness &#8212; which, as <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/09/23/george-eliot-happiness/\">George Eliot well knew</a>, is a skill we incrementally master as we grow older &#8212; sadness, May reminds us, is also a skill: There are self-punishing ways to be sad, and self-salving ways to be sad. In skillful wintering, we learn the difference between the two. Rilke, who wintered amply and wisely, knew that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/03/10/rilke-letters-to-a-young-poet-sadness/\">great sadnesses clarify us to ourselves</a> &#8212; winters of the spirit come in various sizes and cycles, each meaningful, all cumulative in their soul-sculpting beneficence. May writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>When you start tuning in to winter, you realise that we live through a thousand winters in our lives &#8212; some big, some small&#8230; Some winters creep up on us so slowly that they have infiltrated every part of our lives before we truly feel them.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>To get better at wintering, we need to address our very notion of time. We tend to imagine that our lives are linear, but they are in fact cyclical.</p></blockquote>\n<p>This cyclical nature of the seasons of the spirit is counter to our dominant cultural narrative of self-improvement, with its ethos of linear progression toward   states of ever-increasing flourishing. It is counter, too, to the world&#8217;s major spiritual traditions, with their ideas of salvation and enlightenment. (Any longtime practitioner of Zen or metta meditation, for instance, knows that while we do reach moments of so-called enlightenment &#8212; a gladsome dissolution of the self into an all-pervading lovingkindness &#8212; these moments are inevitably punctuated by visitations of our habitual tendencies toward egoic shortness of temper, the self-absorption we call melancholy, and other conditioned modes of unenlightened conduct.) And yet befriending this cyclical rhythm of our inner lives, May observes with life-tested clarity, is the key to wintering &#8212; to emerging from the coldest seasons of the soul not only undiminished but revitalized.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72869\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/everafter4601789_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/EverAfter_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=680%2C343&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"343\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72869\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/EverAfter_by_MariaPopova.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/EverAfter_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=240%2C121&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/EverAfter_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=320%2C162&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/EverAfter_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=768%2C388&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/EverAfter_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=600%2C303&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Ever/After</em> by Maria Popova. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/everafter4601789_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Drawing on the analogy of tress &#8212; these most fertile metaphors for our humanity, in which we <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/08/06/trees-at-night-art-young/\">see ourselves</a> and see quiet wisdom on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/05/04/natascha-mcelhone-wander-hesse-kew/\">how to live with ourselves</a>, on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/11/13/robert-macfarlane-underland-tree-love/\">how to live with each other</a>, on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/09/11/martin-buber-tree/\">the root of authenticity</a>, on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/09/24/paul-klee-tree-artist-creativity/\">what it means to be an artist</a> and <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/10/27/dylan-thomas-being-but-men/\">what it means to be human</a> &#8212; she writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>We are in the habit of imagining our lives to be linear, a long march from birth to death in which we mass our powers, only to surrender them again, all the while slowly losing our youthful beauty. This is a brutal untruth. Life meanders like a path through the woods. We have seasons when we flourish and seasons when the leaves fall from us, revealing our bare bones. Given time, they grow again.</p></blockquote>\n<p>In one of the book&#8217;s wonderful portals into the world of science as a means of comprehending our elemental humanity, May considers the astonishing actuality of trees beyond the merely metaphorical:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The dropping of leaves by deciduous trees is called abscission. It occurs on the cusp between autumn and winter, as part of an arc of growth, maturity, and renewal. In spring and summer, leaf cells are full of chlorophyll, a bright green substance that absorbs sunlight, fueling the process that converts carbon dioxide and water into the starch and sugar that allow the tree to grow. But at the end of the summer, as the days grow shorter and the temperature falls, deciduous trees stop making food. In the absence of sunlight, it becomes too costly to maintain the machinery of growth. The chlorophyll begins to break down, revealing other colours that were always present in the leaf, but which were masked by the abundance of green pigment: oranges and yellows, derived from carotene and xanthophyll. Other chemical changes take place to create red anthocyanin pigments. The exact mix is different for each tree, sometimes producing bright yellows, oranges, and browns, and sometimes displaying as reds or purples.</p>\n<p>But while this is happening, a layer of cells is weakening between the stem and the branch: this is called the abscission zone. Gradually it severs the leaf from access to water, and the leaf dries and browns and in most cases falls off, either under its own weight or encouraged by wintery rains and winds. Within a few hours, the tree will have released substances to heal the scar the leaf has left, protecting itself from the evaporation of water, infection, or the invasion of parasites.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72867\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/alive4601335_print?sku=s6-19355251p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alive_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=680%2C797&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"797\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72867\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alive_by_MariaPopova.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alive_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=240%2C281&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alive_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=320%2C375&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alive_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=768%2C900&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/Alive_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=600%2C704&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Sundown Poem</em> by Maria Popova. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/alive4601335_print?sku=s6-19355251p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>I have always cherished the bare beauty of winter trees, so fractal and pulmonary against the somber sky &#8212; so skeletal, yet so alive. Anyone willing to look  closely &#8212; and why be alive at all if not to relish the ecstasy of noticing, that crowning glory of our consciousness? &#8212; is rewarded with the gasping recognition that the branches are already covered in tiny dormant buds encoding the Braille promise of spring.</p>\n<p>May writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Most trees produce their buds in high summer, and the autumn leaf fall reveals them, neat and expectant, protected from the cold by thick scales&#8230; from the sharp talons of the beech to the hooflike black buds of the ash. Many trees also display catkins in the winter, like the acid-green lambs’ tails of the hazel and the furry grey nubs of the willow. These employ the wind or insects to spread pollen, ready for the new year.</p>\n<p>The tree is waiting. It has everything ready. Its fallen leaves are mulching the forest floor, and its roots are drawing up the extra winter moisture, providing a firm anchor against seasonal storms. Its ripe cones and nuts are providing essential food in this scarce time for mice and squirrels, and its bark is hosting hibernating insects and providing a source of nourishment for hungry deer. It is far from dead. It is in fact the life and soul of the wood. It’s just getting on with it quietly. It will not burst into life in the spring. It will just put on a new coat and face the world again.</p></blockquote>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/goodbye-summer-from-trees-at-night-by-art-young_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/artyoung_treesatnight13.jpg?resize=680%2C1023&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1023\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-68428\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/artyoung_treesatnight13.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/artyoung_treesatnight13.jpg?resize=240%2C361&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/artyoung_treesatnight13.jpg?resize=320%2C482&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/artyoung_treesatnight13.jpg?resize=768%2C1156&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/artyoung_treesatnight13.jpg?resize=600%2C903&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art from <a href=\"\"><em>Trees at Night</em></a> by Art Young, 1926. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/goodbye-summer-from-trees-at-night-by-art-young_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Looking back on her own barren-branched seasons of the soul, she reflects:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Here is another truth about wintering: you’ll find wisdom in your winter, and once it’s over, it’s your responsibility to pass it on. And in return, it’s our responsibility to listen to those who have wintered before us. It’s an exchange of gifts in which nobody loses out. This may involve the breaking of a lifelong habit, one passed down carefully through generations: that of looking at other people’s misfortunes and feeling certain that they brought them upon themselves in a way that you never would. This isn’t just an unkind attitude. It does us harm, because it keeps us from learning that disasters do indeed happen and how we can adapt when they do. It stops us from reaching out to those who are suffering. And when our own disaster comes, it forces us into a humiliated retreat, as we try to hunt down mistakes that we never made in the first place or wrongheaded attitudes that we never held. Either that, or we become certain that there must be someone out there we can blame. Watching winter and really listening to its messages, we learn that effect is often disproportionate to cause; that tiny mistakes can lead to huge disasters; that life is often bloody unfair, but it carries on happening with or without our consent. We learn to look more kindly on other people’s crises, because they are so often portents of our own future.</p></blockquote>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/02/29/arthur-rackham-brothers-grimm/\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/02/arthurrackham_grimm5.jpg\"></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Arthur Rackham for a <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/02/29/arthur-rackham-brothers-grimm/\">rare 1917 edition</a> of the Brothers Grimm fairy tales. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-by-arthur-rackham-from-a-rare-1917-edition-of-the-brothers-grimm-fairy-tales_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The whole of <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Wintering-Power-Retreat-Difficult-Times/dp/0593189485/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_&#34;blank&#34;\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Wintering</em></strong></a> &#8212; which explores the biological, psychological, neurochemical, and philosophical subtleties of our state of being in winter the season and winter the metaphor &#8212; is a splendid and soul-salving read. Complement it with Thoreau&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/01/05/thoreau-excusrsions-a-winter-walk/\">transcendentalist strategy for finding inner warmth in the cold of life</a>, Annie Dillard on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/12/21/annie-dillard-winter-solstice/\">how winter awakens us to life</a>, Adam Gopnik&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/12/21/adam-gopnik-winter/\">lyrical love letter to the white season</a>, and D.H. Lawrence on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/07/21/d-h-lawrence-aarons-rod-cypress-trees/\">trees, solitude, and how we root ourselves when our worlds collapse</a>, then savor more of May&#8217;s writing and the personal story from which it springs in her wonderful <a href=\"https://onbeing.org/programs/katherine-may-how-wintering-replenishes/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>On Being</em> conversation</a> with Krista Tippett.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your life more livable in any way, please consider aiding its sustenance with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/donate/\">donation</a>.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p>Brain Pickings has a free weekly newsletter.
