12:48:46","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:48:46","title":"A Scientist’s Advice on Healing: A Soulful Animated Poem About Getting to the Other Side of Heartbreak","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=72775","description":"<h3>&#8220;Try to accept this fat red hurt is your starting point.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Messenger-Christy-Ducker/dp/1910367966/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"383\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/messenger_christyducker.jpg?fit=320%2C383&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"A Scientist&#8217;s Advice on Healing: A Soulful Animated Poem About Getting to the Other Side of Heartbreak\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/messenger_christyducker.jpg?w=717&#38;ssl=1 717w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/messenger_christyducker.jpg?resize=240%2C288&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/messenger_christyducker.jpg?resize=320%2C383&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/messenger_christyducker.jpg?resize=600%2C719&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>&#8220;Love your heart. For this is the prize,&#8221; Toni Morrison wrote in an exquisite passage from <em>Beloved</em> as she considered <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/01/03/toni-morrison-beloved-heart/\">the body as an instrument of sanity, joy, and self-respect</a> a century after William James asserted in his groundbreaking work on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/01/11/what-is-an-emotion-william-james/\">how our bodies affect our feelings</a> that &#8220;a purely disembodied human emotion is a nonentity,&#8221; lending the fledgling credibility of a young science to Walt Whitman&#8217;s poetic insistence that &#8220;the body includes and is the meaning, the main concern and includes and is the soul.&#8221; </p>\n<p>There is such fertile ground for sensemaking in <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/01/02/the-snail-with-the-right-heart/\">this space between biology and metaphor</a> that we have always used our bodies as sensemaking instruments for the soul. But no part of the body has taken on more metaphorical meaning than the vital organ depicted in millennia of literature and song as the seat of love. </p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/11/29/paul-sougy/\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/sougy_heart.jpg?resize=680%2C900&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"900\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-69334\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/sougy_heart.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/sougy_heart.jpg?resize=240%2C318&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/sougy_heart.jpg?resize=320%2C424&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/sougy_heart.jpg?resize=768%2C1017&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/sougy_heart.jpg?resize=600%2C795&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>The Human Heart</em>. One of French artist Paul Sougy&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/11/29/paul-sougy/\">mid-century scientific diagrams of life</a>. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/paul-sougy-the-human-heart-1950s-proceeds-benefit-the-nature-conservancy_print?sku=s6-11999031p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\">as a print</a> and <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\">as a face mask</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>When we speak of the heart breaking, we are speaking metaphorically, and yet anyone who has lived through heartbreak &#8212; that is, anyone who has lived at all &#8212; knows intimately the awful way in which the psychological condition of loss takes on the quality of physical pain. It is hardly surprising, then, that the body and the soul <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/06/20/the-body-keeps-the-score-van-der-kolk/\">heal in consanguinity</a> &#8212; the heart-as-metaphor heals the same way the heart-as-organ does.</p>\n<p>That is what English poet <a href=\"https://www.christyducker.co.uk/\" target=\"_blank\">Christy Ducker</a> explores with uncommon sensitivity and lyric splendor in &#8220;A Scientist&#8217;s Advice on Healing.&#8221; A fine poet and a fine scholar who earned her Ph.D. while composing <a href=\"https://www.christyducker.co.uk/poems/\" target=\"_blank\">poems</a> about the Victorian lighthouse keeper Grace Darling, Ducker embodies the animating spirit of <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/the-universe-in-verse/\"><em>The Universe in Verse</em></a> and stands as a testament to Ursula K. Le Guin&#8217;s lovely insistence that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/04/10/ursula-k-le-guin-late-in-the-day-science-poetry/\">&#8220;science describes accurately from outside, poetry describes accurately from inside, [and] both celebrate what they describe.&#8221;</a> </p>\n<p>In this enchanting animated poem, Ducker joins visions with artist <a href=\"https://thumbprod.wordpress.com/\" target=\"_blank\">Kate Sweeney</a> to deliver a soulful prescription partway between science and metaphor, between organ and instrument, as palliating to the physiology of illness as it is to the psychology of heartbreak: </p>\n<p><iframe loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://player.vimeo.com/video/163933380?dnt=1&#38;app_id=122963\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"autoplay; fullscreen; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen title=\"A Scientist&#38;#039;s Advice on Healing\"></iframe></p>\n<blockquote><p><strong>A SCIENTIST&#8217;S ADVICE ON HEALING</strong><br />\n<em>by Christy Ducker</em></p>\n<p>Try to accept<br />\nthis fat red hurt<br />\nis your starting point,<br />\nin the way a pen must be put to paper<br />\n&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;in one particular spot,</p>\n<p>then move</p>\n<p>beyond<br />\nthe globby flap<br />\nof blame<br />\n&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;and past<br />\n&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;the mono-sulk<br />\n&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;of pain.</p>\n<p>Change the subject,<br />\nbefore it&#8217;s too late.<br />\nSketch out<br />\nwhat health<br />\nyou do possess,<br />\nwhat signal-cascades,<br />\nwhat flotilla of cells<br />\ncircumnavigate you,</p>\n<p>then draw yourself back<br />\n&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;together again,<br />\nin a language<br />\n&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;of your own.</p>\n<p>Your body&#8217;s talk<br />\nis loose as lymph &#8212;<br />\nit&#8217;ll have you open out<br />\n&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;as a tree,<br />\nor sneak up on pain<br />\n&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;as assassin,<br />\n&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;sidekick,<br />\n&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;or wolf.</p>\n<p>Encourage this<br />\nfor healing won&#8217;t come at you<br />\n&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;straight.<br />\nEmbrace the lack of heroics &#8212;<br />\nthis isn&#8217;t Hollywood,<br />\nit&#8217;s you,<br />\nin a plot<br />\nthat may<br />\nor may not resolve.</p></blockquote>\n<p>The poem appears in <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Messenger-Christy-Ducker/dp/1910367966/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><strong><em>Messenger</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://poetrybusiness.co.uk/product/messenger/\" target=\"_blank\"><em>UK edition</em></a>) &#8212; a slim collection of Ducker&#8217;s poems exploring &#8220;how we wound and how we heal,&#8221; drawing on the science of immunology in a collaboration with York&#8217;s Center for Chronic Disease, and featuring visual poetics by Sweeney, who also animated poet Linda France&#8217;s magnificent <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/01/29/murmuration-linda-france/\">&#8220;Murmuration.&#8221;</a> </p>\n<p>Couple with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/04/10/antidotes-to-fear-of-death-rebecca-elson/\">&#8220;Antidotes to Fear of Death&#8221;</a> &#8212; astronomer and poet Rebecca Elson&#8217;s stunning cosmic salve for our creaturely tremblings of heart &#8212; then revisit Epictetus&#8217;s 2,000-year-old <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/08/26/epictetus-love-loss/\">Stoic strategy for surviving heartbreak</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your life more livable in any way, please consider aiding its sustenance with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/donate/\">donation</a>.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p>Brain Pickings has a free weekly newsletter. Wisdom the Forgotten Book That Shaped the Modern Environmental Movement\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/roadtosurvival_vogt.jpg?w=900&#38;ssl=1 900w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/roadtosurvival_vogt.jpg?resize=240%2C378&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/roadtosurvival_vogt.jpg?resize=320%2C504&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/roadtosurvival_vogt.jpg?resize=768%2C1210&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/roadtosurvival_vogt.jpg?resize=600%2C945&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>A century after the trailblazing conservationist John Muir observed that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/05/10/john-muir-nature-writings/\">&#8220;when we try to pick out anything by itself, we find it hitched to everything else in the universe,&#8221;</a> and half a century before Maya Angelou urged us in her <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/05/09/a-brave-and-startling-truth-maya-angelou/\">cosmic clarion call</a> to see that &#8220;we, this people, on this minuscule and kithless globe&#8221; must correct our course before we destroy ourselves and our kith-hitched globe, the ecologist and conservationist <strong>William Vogt</strong> (May 15, 1902&#8211;July 11, 1968) composed a masterwork of admonition and actionable vision that shaped the ethos of the modern environmental movement and emboldened the generation of pioneers who set it into motion.</p>\n<p>During his long recovery from paralytic polio as a child, William had fallen in love with the natural world, escaping his confinement through books about the wilderness and its wondrous creatures. A century before the Oxford Children&#8217;s Dictionary <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/06/17/the-lost-words-macfarlane-morris/\">discarded dozens of words related to nature</a> as irrelevant to the imagination and its prosthesis in language, the small bedridden boy grew especially enchanted by the feathered creatures of free flight that he met on the page. </p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/06/17/the-lost-words-macfarlane-morris/\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/06/thelostwords7.jpg\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Jackie Morris from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/06/17/the-lost-words-macfarlane-morris/\"><em>The Lost Words</em></a> by Robert Macfarlane</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Literature remained his portal into life as he set out on a literary career in New York. But nature beckoned, the birds beckoned. </p>\n<p>At thirty, Vogt abruptly left the city for Latin America, traveling on a Peruvian commission to study bird populations on the guano islands. In the three years he spent there, laboring in the salty air on the hot barren rocks, he arrived at an empirical proof of Muir&#8217;s insight &#8212; Vogt discovered that when changes in ocean currents diminished the population of plankton and anchovies, millions of birds fled the islands in search of food, leaving their defenseless chicks to die in &#8220;pitiful, collapsed, downy clumps&#8221; that broke his heart. </p>\n<p>He saw in this heartbreak a miniature of the whole &#8212; the intricate interlacing of creaturely destinies on a planet of finite resources, growing populations, and infinite interconnectedness of needs. </p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/12/05/if-you-come-to-earth-sophie-blackall/\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/IYCTE.Birds_.2000.jpg\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/12/05/if-you-come-to-earth-sophie-blackall/\"><em>If You Come to Earth</em></a> by Sophie Blackall</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Vogt spent the next decade and a half developing these ideas by devouring countless books and scientific papers, talking with scientists and sea captains, farmers and diplomats, presidents and sheepherders in Patagonia, engineers and trappers in Manitoba. In 1948 &#8212; the year the great nature writer Henry Beston cast his poetic hope that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/06/01/henry-beston-northern-farm-human-nature/\">&#8220;perhaps there is still time to take a stand for the Kingdom of Life [which] needs defenders&#8221;</a> and that &#8220;perhaps, mighty as its enemies may be, allies will come who are even mightier” &#8212; Vogt distilled his learnings in <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Road-Survival-William-Vogt/dp/1166135950/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><strong><em>Road to Survival</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/road-to-survival/oclc/1057726082&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\"><em>public library</em></a>), a mighty manifesto that roused a generation of allies to stand for the Kingdom of Life. </p>\n<p>At the crux of his inquiry into the key motive forces of our civilization&#8217;s course is Vogt&#8217;s insistence that while much is broken with the exploitive consumerism behind the world&#8217;s government and industry, much more depends on and is mendable by the concerted collective action of ordinary people. In a humbling testament to the slow work of cultural change and civilizational course-correction, it would take nearly a century for his ideas to come alive and actionable in such pillars of ecological responsibility as the Paris Agreement, the Green New Deal, and Greta Thunberg&#8217;s global school climate strike movement. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72765\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/williamvogt.jpg?resize=680%2C622&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"622\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72765\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/williamvogt.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/williamvogt.jpg?resize=240%2C220&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/williamvogt.jpg?resize=320%2C293&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/williamvogt.jpg?resize=768%2C703&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/williamvogt.jpg?resize=600%2C549&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">William Vogt</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In an era when humanity regarded the rest of nature as <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/05/10/america-ferrera-sojourns-in-the-parallel-world-denise-levertov/\">a world parallel to our own</a> &#8212; a world at best visited in pleasant excursions, at worst reduced to extractable resources to serve human needs &#8212; Vogt insists that &#8220;ecological health is one of the indispensables&#8221; in the &#8220;flowering of human happiness and well-being.&#8221; A century after Ernst Haeckel <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/03/26/ernst-haeckel-medusae/\">coined the term <em>ecology</em></a> and a decade before Rachel Carson <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/01/27/rachel-carson-silent-spring-dorothy-freeman/\">made it a household word</a>, Vogt draws on his island discovery to contour the totality of Earth&#8217;s ecological interdependence:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Drastic measures are inescapable. Above everything else, we must reorganize our thinking. If we are to escape the crash we must abandon all thought of living unto ourselves. We form an earth-company, and the lot of the Indiana farmer can no longer be isolated from that of the Bantu&#8230; An eroding hillside in Mexico or Yugoslavia affects the living standard and probability of survival of the American people&#8230; Today&#8217;s white bread may force a break in the levees, and flood New Orleans next spring. This year&#8217;s wheat from Australia&#8217;s eroding slopes may flare into a Japanese war three decades hence.</p></blockquote>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/12/05/if-you-come-to-earth-sophie-blackall/\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/IYCTE.weather.2000.jpg\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/12/05/if-you-come-to-earth-sophie-blackall/\"><em>If You Come to Earth</em></a> by Sophie Blackall</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Rising from the wakeful pages is the assurance, at once empowering and disquieting with its weight of responsibility, that &#8220;we the people&#8221; is not some agglomeration of abstract others but the sum total of each and every one of us as individual and concrete agents of change. </p>\n<p>In a chapter aptly titled &#8220;History of Our Future,&#8221; Vogt writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>When I write &#8220;we&#8221; I do not mean the other fellow. I mean every person who reads a newspaper printed on pulp from vanishing forests. I mean every man and woman who eats a meal drawn from steadily shrinking lands. Everyone who flushes a toilet, and thereby pollutes a river, wastes fertile organic matter and helps to lower a water table. Everyone who puts on a wool garment derived from overgrazed ranges that have been cut by the little hoofs and gullied by the rains, sending runoff and topsoil into the rivers downstream, flooding cities hundreds of miles away.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Writing shortly before he became National Director of Planned Parenthood &#8212; a position he would hold for more than a decade in parallel with his conservation work &#8212; Vogt adds:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Especially do I mean men and women in overpopulated countries who produce excessive numbers of children who, unhappily, cannot escape their fate as hostages to the forces of misery and disaster that lower upon the horizon of our future.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>The direction of these curves and the misery they write across the earth are not likely to be changed in the proximate future. Their direction is fixed for some decades. Great masses of people have a preponderantly young population; as they come into the breeding age we must, despite all possible efforts short of generalized slaughter, expect human numbers to increase for a time. The drag imposed by ignorance, selfishness, nationalism, custom, etc., is certain to retard, by some decades, any effective or substantial improvement of resource management.</p></blockquote>\n<p>In an admonition of astonishing prescience, Vogt insists that changing the trend requires revising our past ideals to calibrate them to an evolving ecological reality:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The freebooting, rugged individualist, whose vigor, imagination, and courage contributed so much of good to the building of our country (along with the bad), we must now recognize, where his activities destroy resources, as the Enemy of the People he has become&#8230; Above all, we must learn to know &#8212; to feel to the core of our beings &#8212; our dependence upon the earth and the riches with which it sustains us. We can no longer believe valid our assumption that we live in independence.</p></blockquote>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/06/04/wangari-maathai-the-woman-who-planted-millions-of-trees/\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/06/wangarimaathai4.jpg\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Aurélia Fronty from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/06/04/wangari-maathai-the-woman-who-planted-millions-of-trees/\"><em>Wangari Maathai: The Woman Who Planted Millions of Trees</em></a> by Franck Prévot</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Writing shortly before Rachel Carson penned her prescient open letter to America, insisting that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/02/08/rachel-carson-washington-post-letter-1953/\">&#8220;the real wealth of the Nation lies in the resources of the earth &#8212; soil, water, forests, minerals, and wildlife,&#8221;</a> Vogt calls for long-term thinking and broad-range feeling:</p>\n<blockquote><p>We must &#8212; all of us, men, women, and children &#8212; reorient ourselves with relation to the world in which we live&#8230; We must come to understand our past, our history, in terms of the soil and water and forests and grasses that have made it what it is. We must see the years to come in the frame that makes space and time one.</p></blockquote>\n<p>In a world he considered already overcrowded and resource-strained by the two billion people inhabiting it &#8212; a population that would triple within a generation &#8212; Vogt adds:</p>\n<blockquote><p>As we are crowded together&#8230; on the shrinking surface of the globe, we have set in motion historical forces that are directed by our total environment.</p></blockquote>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/01/02/the-snail-with-the-right-heart/\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/thesnailwiththerightheart_comet.jpg\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Ping Zhu from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/01/02/the-snail-with-the-right-heart/\"><em>The Snail with the Right Heart</em></a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>Half a century after Alfred Russel Wallace issued his <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/12/11/the-wonderful-century-alfred-russel-wallace/\">prophetic prescription for civilizational course-correction</a> &#8212; an admonition that fell on deaf ears at the outset of the twentieth century and would remain a point of willful deafness in the climate denial of the twenty-first &#8212; Vogt makes an impassioned and empowering appeal to the only substantive force of change in the grand scheme of any society and civilization:</p>\n<blockquote><p>If we ourselves do not govern our destiny, firmly and courageously, no one is going to do it for us. To regain ecological freedom for our civilization will be a heavy task. It will frequently require arduous and uncomfortable measures. It will cost considerable sums of money. Democratic governments are not likely to set forth on such a steep and rocky path unless people lead the way.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>So that the people shall not delude themselves, find further frustration through quack nostrums, fight their way into blind alleys, it is imperative that this world-wide dilemma be made known to all mankind. The human race is caught in a situation as concrete as a pair of shoes two sizes too small. We must understand that, and stop blaming economic systems, the weather, bad luck, or callous saints. This is the beginning of wisdom, and the first step on the long road back.</p></blockquote>\n<p>For a contemporary counterpart to Vogt&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Road-Survival-William-Vogt/dp/1166135950/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><strong><em>Road to Survival</em></strong></a>, see the excellent anthology of policy, poetry, and science <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/All-We-Can-Save-Solutions/dp/0593237064/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><em>All We Can Save: Truth, Courage, and Solutions for the Climate Crisis</em></a>, shining a kaleidoscope of actionable perspective by women leading the way on the road Vogt envisioned, then revisit Eve Ensler&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/10/28/eve-ensler-apology-mother-earth/\">extraordinary letter of apology to Mother Earth</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. 12:48:46","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:48:46","title":"A Cenotaph for Newton: The Poetry of Public Spaces, the Architecture of Shadow, and How Trees Inspired the World’s First Planetarium Design","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=72972","description":"<h3>How a forgotten visionary&#8217;s futuristic dream dared generations to reimagine the relationship between nature and human creativity. </h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Boullee-Visionary-Architecture-Including-Boullees/dp/0517525690/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"417\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_architectureart.jpg?fit=320%2C417&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"A Cenotaph for Newton: The Poetry of Public Spaces, the Architecture of Shadow, and How Trees Inspired the World&#8217;s First Planetarium Design\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_architectureart.jpg?w=1689&#38;ssl=1 1689w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_architectureart.jpg?resize=320%2C417&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_architectureart.jpg?resize=600%2C782&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_architectureart.jpg?resize=240%2C313&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_architectureart.jpg?resize=768%2C1000&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_architectureart.jpg?resize=1179%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1179w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_architectureart.jpg?resize=1572%2C2048&#38;ssl=1 1572w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_architectureart.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>Nineteen years after the publication of Isaac Newton&#8217;s epoch-making <em>Principia</em> &#8212; in England, in Latin &#8212; the prodigy mathematician <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/01/03/emilie-du-chatelet-fable-of-the-bees-preface/\">Émilie du Châtelet</a> set out to translate his ideas into her native French, making them more comprehensible in the process. Her more-than-translation &#8212; which includes several of her mathematical corrections and clarifications of Newton&#8217;s imprecisions, and which remains the only comprehensive edition in French to this day &#8212; popularized his ideas in France and, from this epicenter of the Enlightenment, spread them centripetally throughout the rest of the Continent, rendering Newton himself an emblem of the Enlightenment the sweep of which he never lived to see. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_70339\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/04/blake_newton.jpg?w=680&#038;ssl=1\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Newton</em> by William Blake (Tate Britain)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Not long after Du Châtelet&#8217;s untimely death, her legacy reached one of her most gifted compatriots &#8212; the visionary architect <strong>Étienne-Louis Boullée</strong> (February 12, 1728&#8211;February 4, 1799), who fell under Newton&#8217;s spell. Determined to honor Newton with a worthy cenotaph &#8212; a memorial tomb for a person buried elsewhere &#8212; he designed a sphere 500 feet in diameter, taller than the Pyramids of Giza, nested into a colossal pedestal and encircled by hundreds of cypress trees, giving it the transfixing illusion of being both half-buried into the Earth and hovering unmoored from gravity. It was also, in essence, the world&#8217;s first domed planetarium design.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72976\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph7.jpg?resize=680%2C411&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"411\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72976\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph7.jpg?w=1325&#38;ssl=1 1325w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph7.jpg?resize=320%2C193&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph7.jpg?resize=600%2C363&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph7.jpg?resize=240%2C145&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph7.jpg?resize=768%2C464&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image courtesy of Bibliothèque nationale de France.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The cenotaph was a touching gesture in the first place &#8212; a Frenchman honoring a genius born of and interred in England, a nation with which Boullée&#8217;s own had been in near-ceaseless war for centuries, with those tensions at an all-time high at the time of his design, thanks to the American Revolutionary War. Doubly touching was his choice of a sphere: One of Newton&#8217;s most revolutionary contributions &#8212; the mathematical inference that because gravity is weaker at the equator, the shape of the Earth must be spherical &#8212; had defied France&#8217;s greatest son, René Descartes, who maintained that the Earth was egg-shaped. When Boullée was still a boy, a young Frenchman &#8212; Émilie du Châtelet&#8217;s mathematics tutor &#8212; had joined a perilous Arctic expedition to prove Newton correct. Two centuries later, in the wake of the world&#8217;s grimmest war yet, <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/10/29/in-transit-neil-gaiman-eddington/\">a queer Quaker Englishman would do the same</a>, risking his life to defend the epoch-making theory of a German Jew &#8212; the theory of relativity that ultimately subverted Newton. Another world war later, Einstein himself would appeal to what he called <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/04/27/albert-einstein-the-common-language-of-science/\">&#8220;the common language of science&#8221;</a> &#8212; that truth-seeking contact with nature and reality that transcends all borders and all nationalisms, the impulse that animated Boullée&#8217;s bold homage to Newton.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72978\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph5.jpg?resize=680%2C655&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"655\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72978\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph5.jpg?w=1067&#38;ssl=1 1067w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph5.jpg?resize=320%2C308&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph5.jpg?resize=600%2C578&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph5.jpg?resize=240%2C231&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph5.jpg?resize=768%2C739&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Cenotaph side cross-section. Image courtesy of Bibliothèque nationale de France.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>While governed by the credo that &#8220;our buildings &#8212; and our public buildings in particular &#8212; should be to some extent poems,&#8221; Boullée also believed that science could magnify the poetry of public spaces, which must at bottom reflect the principles of the grand designer: Nature. A century before the teenage Virginia Woolf wrote that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/01/14/virginia-woolf-on-imitation-and-the-arts/\">&#8220;all the Arts&#8230; imitate as far as they can the one great truth that all can see,&#8221;</a> Boullée insisted:</p>\n<blockquote><p>No idea exists that does not derive from nature&#8230; It is impossible to create architectural imagery without a profound knowledge of nature: the Poetry of architecture lies in natural effects. That is what makes architecture an art and that art sublime.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Architecture in the modern sense was then a young art, because <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/01/02/perspective/\">the art-science of perspective was so novel</a>. Newton&#8217;s optics, derived directly from the laws of nature, had revolutionized it all. Boullée came to define architecture as &#8220;the art of creating perspectives by the arrangement of volumes,&#8221; but a highly poetic art: </p>\n<blockquote><p>The real talent of an architect lies in incorporating in his work the sublime attraction of Poetry.</p></blockquote>\n<p>The poetry of architecture, he argued, resides in using perspective and light in such a way that &#8220;our senses are reminded of nature.&#8221; He interpreted the laws of nature, as clarified by Newton&#8217;s optics and mathematics, to intimate that no shape embodies this serenade to the senses with greater power and precision than the sphere:</p>\n<blockquote><p>A sphere is, in all respects, the image of perfection. It combines strict symmetry with the most perfect regularity and the greatest possible variety; its form is developed to the fullest extent and is the simplest that exists; its shape is outlined by the most agreeable contour and, finally, the light effects that it produces are so beautifully graduated that they could not possibly be softer, more agreeable or more varied. These unique advantages, which the sphere derives from nature, have an immeasurable hold over our senses.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72981\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph2.jpg?resize=680%2C404&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"404\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72981\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph2.jpg?w=1297&#38;ssl=1 1297w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph2.jpg?resize=320%2C190&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph2.jpg?resize=600%2C356&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph2.jpg?resize=240%2C142&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph2.jpg?resize=768%2C456&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image courtesy of Bibliothèque nationale de France.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>And so Boullée predicated his cenotaph for Newton on an enormous sphere that would convey his ultimate intent for the temple &#8212; to arouse in the visitor&#8217;s soul &#8220;feelings in keeping with religious ceremonies,&#8221; a sense of grandeur leaving them &#8220;moved by such an excess of sensibility&#8230; that all the faculties of our soul are disturbed to such an extent that we feel it is departing from our body&#8221; &#8212; an effect always best achieved not by an enormity of sheer size and space but by a considered contrast of scales. No building, he observed, &#8220;calls for the Poetry of architecture&#8221; more than a memorial to the dead. Believing that architecture, like all art, should ultimately serve to enlarge our sense of aliveness, and that we are never more alive than when we are rooted in our creaturely senses, Boullée insisted that the key to this sense of grandeur lies in applying the principles of nature&#8217;s mathematics with poetic subtlety &#8212; the principles laid bare in the <em>Principia</em>, the principles that &#8220;derive from order, the symbol of wisdom.&#8221; He wrote: </p>\n<blockquote><p>Symmetry&#8230; is what results from the order that extends in every direction and multiplies them at our glance until we can no longer count them. By extending the sweep of an avenue so that its end is out of sight, the laws of optics and the effects of perspective given an impression of immensity; at each step, the objects appear in a new guise and our pleasure is renewed by a succession of different vistas. Finally, by some miracle which in fact is the result of our own movement but which we attribute to the objects around us, the latter seem to move with us, as if we had imparted Life to them.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72975\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph1.jpg?resize=680%2C667&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"667\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72975\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph1.jpg?w=1041&#38;ssl=1 1041w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph1.jpg?resize=320%2C314&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph1.jpg?resize=600%2C588&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph1.jpg?resize=240%2C235&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph1.jpg?resize=768%2C753&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Aerial cross-section. Image courtesy of Bibliothèque nationale de France.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>But my favorite part of the story is that Boullée found his formative inspiration, not only for the Newton cenotaph and but for his entire creative philosophy, in an unusual encounter with trees &#8212; those <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/05/04/natascha-mcelhone-wander-hesse-kew/\">profoundest of teachers</a>.</p>\n<p>One evening, heavy with grief, Boullée went for a walk along the edge of a forest. Under the moonlight, he noticed his shadow. He had seen his shadow a thousand times before, but the peculiar lens of his psychic state rendered it entirely new &#8212; a living artwork of &#8220;extreme melancholy.&#8221; Looking around, he saw the shadows of the trees in this new light, too, etching onto the ground the profound drama of life. The entire scene was suddenly awash in &#8220;all that is sombre in nature.&#8221; He had seen the state of his soul mirrored back by the natural world, as we so often do in those rawest moments when we are stripped to the base of our being, grounded into our creaturely senses. </p>\n<p>This was the moment of Boullée&#8217;s artistic awakening &#8212; that moment of revelation when, as Virginia Woolf wrote in her <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/09/09/virginia-woolf-cotton-wool-moments-of-being/\">exquisite account of her own artistic awakening</a>, something lifts &#8220;the cotton wool of daily life&#8221; and we see the familiar world afresh. Boullée recounted:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The mass of objects stood out in black against the extreme wanness of the light. Nature offered itself to my gaze in mourning. I was struck by the sensations I was experiencing and immediately began to wonder how to apply this, especially to architecture. I tried to find a composition made up of the effect of shadows. To achieve this, I imagined the light (as I had observed it in nature) giving back to me all that my imagination could think of. That was how I proceeded when I was seeking to discover this new type of architecture.</p></blockquote>\n<p>He called this new architecture &#8220;the architecture of shadow.&#8221; His vision for Newton&#8217;s cenotaph was its grand testament:</p>\n<blockquote><p>I attempted to create the greatest of all effects, that of immensity; for that is what gives us lofty thoughts as we contemplate the Creator and give us celestial sensations.</p></blockquote>\n<p>He attempted, more than that, to honor Newton on his own terms, by the essence of his genius:</p>\n<blockquote><p>O Newton! With the range of your intelligence and the sublime nature of your Genius, you have defined the shape of the earth; I have conceived the idea of enveloping you with your discovery&#8230; your own self. How can I find outside you anything worthy of you?</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72979\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph4.jpg?resize=680%2C411&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"411\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72979\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph4.jpg?w=1313&#38;ssl=1 1313w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph4.jpg?resize=320%2C193&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph4.jpg?resize=600%2C362&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph4.jpg?resize=240%2C145&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph4.jpg?resize=768%2C464&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image courtesy of Bibliothèque nationale de France.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In a further homage to Newton&#8217;s legacy, with Boullée regarded as a &#8220;divine system&#8221; of laws, he chose to suspend a sole spherical lamp over the tomb as the only decoration in the entire monument &#8212; anything else, he felt, would be &#8220;committing sacrilege.&#8221; The contrast of scales &#8212; the smaller sphere of the lamp inside the enormous sphere of the building &#8212; would dramatize the contrast of light and shadow, just as the moonlight had done that fateful night of artistic revelation by the trees. This would give the visitor the sense that they are &#8220;as if by magic floating in the air, borne in the wake of images in the immensity of space.&#8221; Boullée considered the play of light the vital element in this enchantment:</p>\n<blockquote><p>It is light that produces impressions which arouse in us various contradictory sensations depending on whether they are brilliant or sombre. If I could manage to diffuse in my temple magnificent light effects I would fill the onlooker with joy; but if, on the contrary, my temple had only sombre effects, I would fill him with sadness. If I could avoid direct light and arrange for its presence without the onlooker being aware of its source, the ensuing effect of mysterious daylight would produce inconceivable impression and, in a sense, a truly enchanting magic quality.</p></blockquote>\n<p>At a time long before readily available electric light and light-projection, he leaned on Newton&#8217;s optics to envision something that was part Stonehenge and part Hayden Planetarium. A century and a half before the first modern planetarium dome, Boullée dotted the black interior of his dome with an intricate arrangement of tiny holes reflecting the positions of the constellations and the planets, streaming in daylight to create an enchanting nightscape inside. But unlike the modern counterpart, Boullée&#8217;s was a reversible planetarium &#8212; at night, the sole spherical light would irradiate the tiny holes from the other direction, making the dome appear as a self-contained universe if viewed from above. This, lest we forget, was the golden age of aeronautics, when hot-air balloons first defied gravity to lift the human animal into the sky. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72977\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph6.jpg?resize=680%2C412&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"412\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72977\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph6.jpg?w=1302&#38;ssl=1 1302w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph6.jpg?resize=320%2C194&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph6.jpg?resize=600%2C363&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph6.jpg?resize=240%2C145&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/boullee_newtoncenotaph6.jpg?resize=768%2C465&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Side cross-section. Image courtesy of Bibliothèque nationale de France.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Too visionary for its era, the cenotaph was never built, but Boullée&#8217;s ink-and-wash drawings circulated widely in the final decade of his life, eliciting both gasping admiration and merciless derision &#8212; the fate of the true visionary. With the publication of his <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Boullee-Visionary-Architecture-Including-Boullees/dp/0517525690/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">impassioned and insightful writings</a> nearly two centuries after his death, translated by Helen Rosenau, his vision went on to inspire generations of modern artists and architects with a new way of thinking about the poetry of public spaces and the relationship between nature and human creativity.</p>\n<p>In a sentiment evocative of another pioneer&#8217;s lamentation &#8212; Harriet Hosmer&#8217;s astute remark that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/02/27/harriet-hosmer-figuring/\">&#8220;if one knew but one-half the difficulties an artist has to surmount&#8230; the public would be less ready to censure him for his shortcomings or slow advancement&#8221;</a> &#8212; Boullée wrote of his critics:</p>\n<blockquote><p>No one is more exacting than a man who is not conversant with a given art for he is unable to imagine all the difficulties the artist has to overcome.</p></blockquote>\n<p>His ultimate satisfaction was not the reception or execution of his designs, but the inexhaustible source of their inspiration &#8212; the elemental wellspring of the creative impulse behind all art and all science, that richest and readiest reward of our aliveness:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The artist&#8230; is always making discoveries and spends his life observing nature.</p></blockquote>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your life more livable in any way, please consider aiding its sustenance with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/donate/\">donation</a>.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p>Brain Pickings has a free weekly newsletter. 3 12:48:46","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:48:46","title":"Proximity: A Meditative Visual Poem for Those Reaching for Something They Can’t Quite Grasp, Inspired by Trees","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=72895","description":"<h3>Soulful sylvan consolation partway between David Byrne, Bill T. Jones, and the Buddha. </h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Consolations-Nourishment-Underlying-Meaning-Everyday/dp/1786897636/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"506\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/davidwhyte_consolations.jpg?fit=320%2C506&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Proximity: A Meditative Visual Poem for Those Reaching for Something They Can&#8217;t Quite Grasp, Inspired by Trees\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/davidwhyte_consolations.jpg?w=1618&#38;ssl=1 1618w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/davidwhyte_consolations.jpg?resize=240%2C380&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/davidwhyte_consolations.jpg?resize=320%2C506&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/davidwhyte_consolations.jpg?resize=768%2C1215&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/davidwhyte_consolations.jpg?resize=600%2C949&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/davidwhyte_consolations.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>When I am sad, I like to imagine myself becoming a tree. Branches that bend without breaking, <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/02/22/mandelbrot-fractals-chaos/\">fractal</a> with possibility, reaching resolutely toward the light. Roots touching the web of belonging beneath the surface of the world, that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/07/10/trees-ted-ed/\">majestic mycelial network</a> succoring and nurturing and connecting tree to tree &#8212; connection so effortless, so imperturbable, so free from the fragility of human relationships.</p>\n<p>After writing about wintering trees as <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/03/06/wintering-katherine-may/\">supreme teachers in resilience</a>, I received a lovely note from a reader in England &#8212; theater artist, movement director, and Hatha Yoga teacher <a href=\"https://andrewdawson.info\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Andrew Dawson</a>, a former student of <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/tag/merce-cunningham/\">Merce Cunningham</a>’s. He shared a kindred-spirited film he had made, in his words, &#8220;for those who are reaching for something more but can’t quite grasp it, for those on their journey, not yet at their destination.&#8221;</p>\n<p>It salved me profoundly, this meditative visual poem &#8212; part David Byrne, part Bill T. Jones, and part Buddha &#8212; radiating Hermann Hesse&#8217;s century-old wisdom that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/05/04/natascha-mcelhone-wander-hesse-kew/\">&#8220;whoever has learned how to listen to trees no longer wants to be a tree [but] wants to be nothing except what he is.&#8221;</a></p>\n<p>Commissioned by the <a href=\"https://mimelondon.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">London International Mime Festival</a>, filmed by Dawson&#8217;s son, Roman Sheppard Dawson, and featuring music by composer <a href=\"http://www.jonnypilcher.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Jonny Pilcher</a>, the film was inspired by a line from a short lyrical essay titled &#8220;Close&#8221; from poet and philosopher David Whyte&#8217;s superb collection <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Consolations-Nourishment-Underlying-Meaning-Everyday/dp/1786897636/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Consolations: The Solace, Nourishment and Underlying Meaning of Everyday Words</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"http://www.worldcat.org/title/consolations-the-solace-nourishment-and-the-underlying-meaning/oclc/904413782&#38;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; a book of lyrical reanimations of language that touched me deeply when I <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/11/16/david-whyte-consolations-courage-crisis/\">first read it</a> several years ago (and for the recent English edition of which I had the honor and joy of composing the introduction).</p>\n<blockquote><p>We live by unconsciously measuring the inverse distances of our proximity.</p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe loading=\"lazy\" title=\"Proximity\" src=\"https://player.vimeo.com/video/522773735?dnt=1&#38;app_id=122963\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"autoplay; fullscreen; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>Here is Whyte&#8217;s original mycelium of inspiration for Dawson&#8217;s <em>Proximity</em>:</p>\n<blockquote><p>CLOSE</p>\n<p>is what we almost always are: close to happiness, close to another, close to leaving, close to tears, close to God, close to losing faith, close to being done, close to saying something, or close to success, and even, with the greatest sense of satisfaction, close to giving the whole thing up.</p>\n<p>Our human essence lies not in arrival, but in being almost there, we are creatures who are on the way, our journey a series of impending anticipated arrivals. We live by unconsciously measuring the inverse distances of our proximity: an intimacy calibrated by the vulnerability we feel in giving up our sense of separation.</p>\n<p>To go beyond our normal identities and become closer than close is to lose our sense of self in temporary joy, a form of arrival that only opens us to deeper forms of intimacy that blur our fixed, controlling, surface identity.</p>\n<p>To consciously become close is a courageous form of unilateral disarmament, a chancing of our arm and our love, a willingness to hazard our affections and an unconscious declaration that we might be equal to the inevitable loss that the vulnerability of being close will bring.</p>\n<p>Human beings do not find their essence through fulfillment or eventual arrival but by staying close to the way they like to travel, to the way they hold the conversation between the ground on which they stand and the horizon to which they go. What makes the rainbow beautiful, is not the pot of gold at its end, but the arc of its journey between here and there, between now and then, between where we are now and where we want to go, illustrated above our unconscious heads in primary colour.</p>\n<p>We are in effect, always, close; always close to the ultimate secret: that we are more real in our simple wish to find a way than any destination we could reach: the step between not understanding that and understanding that, is as close as we get to happiness.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Complement Dawson&#8217;s poetic short film with Dylan Thomas&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/10/27/dylan-thomas-being-but-men/\">cinematic poem about how trees illuminate the wonder of our humanity</a> and Robert Macfarlane&#8217;s reflection on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/11/13/robert-macfarlane-underland-tree-love/\">how trees embody the secret to healthy relationships</a>, then revisit Whyte&#8217;s lyrical rerooting of the meanings of <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/11/16/david-whyte-consolations-courage-crisis/\">courage</a>, <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/04/11/david-whyte-vulnerability/\">vulnerability</a>, <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/05/15/david-whyte-consolations-anger-forgiveness-maturity/\">forgiveness</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/04/29/david-whyte-consolations-words/\">love</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your life more livable in any way, please consider aiding its sustenance with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/donate/\">donation</a>.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p>Brain Pickings has a free weekly newsletter.
